       &lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;        &lt;li class="subsection"&gt;&#x000A;          &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-removing_directories" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;4.4 &lt;/span&gt;Renaming, copying, and deleting directories&lt;/a&gt;&#x000A;        &lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;        &lt;li class="subsection"&gt;&#x000A;          &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-summary_directories" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;4.5 &lt;/span&gt;Summary&lt;/a&gt;&#x000A;        &lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;      &lt;/ul&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li class="section"&gt;&#x000A;      &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-conclusion" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;5 &lt;/span&gt;Conclusion&lt;/a&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;  &lt;/ul&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Learn Enough Command Line to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt; is an introduction to the command line for complete beginners, the first in a &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;series of tutorials&lt;/a&gt; designed to teach the common foundations of “computer magic” (&lt;a href="#aside-computer_magic" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) to as broad an audience as possible.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; It is aimed both at those who work with software developers and those who aspire to become developers themselves.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Unlike most introductions to the command line, which typically assume a relatively high level of technical sophistication, &lt;em&gt;Learn Enough Command Line to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt; assumes no prerequisites other than general computer knowledge (how to launch an application, how to use a web browser, how to &lt;a href="http://lmgtfy.com/?q=learn+to+touch+type" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;touch type&lt;/a&gt;, etc.).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Among other things, this means that it doesn’t assume you know &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/text-editor-tutorial" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;how to use a text editor&lt;/a&gt;, or even what a text editor is.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Indeed, this tutorial doesn’t even assume you know what a &lt;em&gt;command line&lt;/em&gt; is, so if you’re confused by the title, you’re still in the right place.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Finally, even if you already know how to use the command line, following this tutorial (and doing the exercises) will help fill in any gaps in your knowledge, and might even teach you a few new things.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A; &lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Note&lt;/em&gt;: To get the most out of this tutorial, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/story" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt;, a subscription service from Learn Enough to Be Dangerous that includes integrated progress tracking, exercise answers, live chat, and streaming videos.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; See &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/story" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/story&lt;/a&gt; for more information.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="aside" id="aside-computer_magic" data-tralics-id="uid1" data-number="1"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Box 1.&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;The magic of computers&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Computers may be as close as we get to &lt;em&gt;magic&lt;/em&gt; in the real world: we type incantations into a machine, and—if the incantations are right—the machine does our bidding.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To perform such magic, computer witches and wizards rely not only on words, but also on wands, potions, and an ancient tome or two.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Taken together, these tricks of the trade are known as &lt;em&gt;software development&lt;/em&gt;: computer programming, plus tools like &lt;em&gt;command lines&lt;/em&gt;, &lt;em&gt;text editors&lt;/em&gt;, and &lt;em&gt;version control&lt;/em&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Knowledge of these tools is perhaps the main dividing line between “technical” and “non-technical” people (or, to put it in magical terms, between magicians and &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muggle" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Muggles&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The present tutorial represents the first step needed to cross this technical/non-technical divide.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The resulting &lt;em&gt;technical sophistication&lt;/em&gt; (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-technical_sophistication" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) will make us software magicians—able to cast computer spells, and get the machine to do our bidding.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;My name is &lt;a href="http://www.michaelhartl.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Michael Hartl&lt;/a&gt;, and I am perhaps best known as the creator of the &lt;a href="http://www.railstutorial.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Ruby on Rails Tutorial&lt;/a&gt;, a &lt;a href="http://railstutorial.org/book" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;book&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="http://screencasts.railstutorial.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;screencast series&lt;/a&gt; that together constitute one of the leading introductions to web development.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (You may also know me, in my more mathematical mode, as the founder of &lt;a href="http://tauday.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Tau Day&lt;/a&gt; and author of &lt;a href="http://tauday.com/tau-manifesto" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;The Tau Manifesto&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; One of the most frequently asked questions about the Rails Tutorial is, “Is the Rails Tutorial good for complete beginners?”&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The answer is, “Not really.”&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; While it is possible for complete beginners to learn web development with the Ruby on Rails Tutorial (and an impressively large number have), it can be challenging and occasionally frustrating, and I don’t generally recommend it.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Instead, I recommend starting here.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;Many programming tutorials either gloss over the command line or assume you already know how to use it.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; But understanding the basics of the command line is &lt;em&gt;absolutely essential&lt;/em&gt; to becoming a skilled developer.&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-1" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-1"&gt;1&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Indeed, if you look at the desktop of an experienced computer programmer, even on a system with a polished graphical user interface like macOS, you are likely to find a large number of “terminal windows”, each containing a series of commands at a command line (&lt;a href="#fig-dev_desktop" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Proficiency at the command line is also useful for anyone who needs to &lt;em&gt;work&lt;/em&gt; with developers, such as product managers, project managers, and designers.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Making this essential component of technical sophistication accessible to as broad an audience as possible is the goal of &lt;em&gt;Learn Enough Command Line to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-dev_desktop" data-tralics-id="uid3" data-number="1"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/dev_desktop.png" alt="images/figures/dev_desktop"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 1: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Terminal windows on the desktop of an experienced developer.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-basics" data-tralics-id="cid1" class="section" data-number="1"&gt;&lt;h2&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-basics" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;1 &lt;/span&gt;Basics&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;As author &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neal_Stephenson" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Neal Stephenson&lt;/a&gt; famously &lt;a href="http://www.cryptonomicon.com/beginning.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;put it&lt;/a&gt;, “In the Beginning was the Command Line.”&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Although a graphical user interface (GUI) can dramatically simplify computer use, in many contexts the most powerful and flexible way to interact with a computer is through a &lt;em&gt;command-line interface&lt;/em&gt; (CLI).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In such an interface, the &lt;a href="http://tron.wikia.com/wiki/User" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;user&lt;/a&gt; types &lt;em&gt;commands&lt;/em&gt; that tell the computer to perform desired tasks.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; These commands can then be combined in various ways to achieve a variety of outcomes.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; An example of a typical command-line command appears in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-command_line_command" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-command_line_command" data-tralics-id="uid4" data-number="2"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/command_line_command.png" alt="images/figures/command_line_command"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 2: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;A prototypical command-line command.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;This tutorial covers the basics of the Unix command line, where &lt;em&gt;Unix&lt;/em&gt; refers to a &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unix" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;family of operating systems&lt;/a&gt; that includes Linux, Android, iOS (iPhone/iPad), and macOS.&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-2" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-2"&gt;2&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Unix systems serve most of the software on the World Wide Web, run most mobile and tablet devices, and power many of the world’s desktop computers as well.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As a result of Unix’s central role in modern computing, this tutorial covers the Unix way of developing software.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The main exception to Unix’s dominance is Microsoft® Windows™, which is not part of the Unix tradition, but those who mostly develop using native Windows development tools will still benefit from learning the Unix command line.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Among other things, at some point such users are likely to need to issue commands on a Unix server (e.g., via the “secure shell” command &lt;code&gt;ssh&lt;/code&gt;), at which point familiarity with Unix commands becomes essential.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As a result, Windows users are strongly encouraged to run a free &lt;em&gt;Linux virtual machine&lt;/em&gt; (as described in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-virtual_machine" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) or to use a &lt;em&gt;cloud IDE&lt;/em&gt;&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-3" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-3"&gt;3&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; such as &lt;a href="http://c9.io/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Cloud9&lt;/a&gt;; to go this latter route, refer to the &lt;a href="https://www.learnenough.com/dev-environment-tutorial#sec-cloud_ide" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Cloud IDE&lt;/a&gt; section in &lt;a href="https://www.learnenough.com/dev-environment-tutorial" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Learn Enough Dev Environment to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="aside" id="aside-virtual_machine" data-tralics-id="uid7" data-number="2"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Box 2.&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Running a virtual machine&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;In order to complete this tutorial, Windows users who don’t want to use the cloud IDE should install a couple of free programs to run a &lt;em&gt;virtual machine&lt;/em&gt; (a simulation of a computer) that allows Windows to host a version of the Linux operating system.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Note&lt;/em&gt;: These steps can be rather tricky, and unfortunately we don’t have the resources to offer individual technical support on virtual machines.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; If you run into trouble, we suggest giving the &lt;a href="https://www.learnenough.com/dev-environment-tutorial#sec-cloud_ide" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;cloud IDE&lt;/a&gt; a try instead.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The steps to install a virtual machine appear as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Install the right version of &lt;a href="https://www.virtualbox.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;VirtualBox&lt;/a&gt; for your system (free).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Download the &lt;a href="https://softcover-static.s3.amazonaws.com/LearnEnough-v.1.4.ova" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Virtual Machine&lt;/a&gt; (large file).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Once the download is complete, double-click the resulting “OVA” file and follow the instructions to install the Virtual Machine (VM).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Double-click the VM itself and log in using the default user’s password, which is “&lt;code class="tt"&gt;foobar!&lt;/code&gt;”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;(Getting all these steps to work is a good exercise in &lt;em&gt;technical sophistication&lt;/em&gt;, an idea we’ll develop further starting in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-man_pages" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1.3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-technical_sophistication" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The result will be a Linux desktop environment (including a command-line terminal program) pre-configured for this tutorial, as shown in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-virtual_machine" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;In the longer run, I recommend switching to a Mac as soon as possible.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; You might have to save up a bit, as Macs are generally more expensive than Windows machines, but in most cases the increased productivity will quickly pay for the difference.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (If you find yourself liking Linux, feel free to stick with it, but Macs are generally easier to use with a better user interface.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Plus, you can always run Linux inside a VM, even on a Mac.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-virtual_machine" data-tralics-id="uid12" data-number="3"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/virtual_machine.png" alt="images/figures/virtual_machine"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 3: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;A Linux virtual machine running inside a host OS.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-running_a_terminal" data-tralics-id="uid13" class="subsection" data-number="1.1"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-running_a_terminal" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;1.1 &lt;/span&gt;Running a terminal&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;To run a command-line command, we first need to start a &lt;em&gt;terminal&lt;/em&gt;, which is the program that gives us a command line.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; On macOS, you can open a terminal window using the macOS application &lt;a href="https://support.apple.com/en-us/HT204014" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Spotlight&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, which you can launch either by typing ⌘␣ (Command-space) or by clicking on the magnifying glass in the upper right part of your screen.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Once you’ve launched Spotlight, you can start a terminal program by typing “terminal” in the Spotlight Search bar.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (If you are interested in using a more advanced and customizable terminal program, I recommend installing &lt;a href="https://www.iterm2.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;iTerm&lt;/a&gt;, but this step is optional.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; On Linux, you can click the terminal icon as shown in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-virtual_machine" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The result should be something like &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-terminal_window" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, although the exact details on your system will likely differ.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; If you’re using a different OS, I recommend applying your technical sophistication (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-technical_sophistication" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) to figure how to open a terminal on your system; for example, to learn how to open a command-line terminal on a &lt;a href="https://www.google.com/chromebook/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Chromebook&lt;/a&gt;, you could Google “&lt;a href="http://lmgtfy.com/?q=how+to+get+a+command+line+on+a+chromebook" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;how to get a command line on a chromebook&lt;/a&gt;”.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-terminal_window" data-tralics-id="uid14" data-number="4"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/terminal_window.png" alt="images/figures/terminal_window"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 4: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;A terminal window.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The example we saw in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-command_line_command" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; includes all of the typical elements of a command, as illustrated in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-anatomy" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;: the &lt;em&gt;prompt&lt;/em&gt; followed by a &lt;em&gt;command&lt;/em&gt; (as in “give the computer a command”), an &lt;em&gt;option&lt;/em&gt; (as in “choose a different option”), and an &lt;em&gt;argument&lt;/em&gt; (as in the “&lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argument_of_a_function" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;argument of a function&lt;/a&gt;” in mathematics).&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-4" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-4"&gt;4&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; It’s essential to understand that the prompt is supplied automatically by the terminal, and you do not need to type it.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (Indeed, if you do type it, it will likely result in an error.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Moreover, the exact details of the prompt will differ, and are not important for the purposes of this tutorial (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-prompt" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-anatomy" data-tralics-id="uid16" data-number="5"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/anatomy.png" alt="images/figures/anatomy"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 5: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Anatomy of a command line.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (Your prompt may differ.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="aside" id="aside-prompt" data-tralics-id="uid17" data-number="3"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Box 3.&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;What is the prompt?&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Every command line starts with some symbol or symbols designed to “prompt” you to action.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The prompt usually ends with a dollar sign &lt;code class="inline_verbatim"&gt;$&lt;/code&gt;, and is preceded by information that depends on the details of your system.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For example, on some systems the prompt might look like this:&#x000A;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;pre&gt; Michael&#x0027;s MacBook Air:~ mhartl$&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;In &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-terminal_window" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, the prompt looks like this instead:&#x000A;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;pre&gt; [~]$&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;and in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-anatomy" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; it looks like this:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; [projects]$&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Finally, the prompt I’m looking at right now looks like this:&#x000A;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;pre&gt; [learn_enough_command_line (master)]$&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;For the purposes of this tutorial, the details of the prompt are not important, but we will discuss useful ways to customize the prompt starting in the next tutorial after this one (&lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/text-editor-tutorial" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Learn Enough Text Editor to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_terminal" data-tralics-id="uid18" class="subsubsection" data-number="1.1.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_terminal" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Learn Enough Command Line to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt; includes a large number of exercises.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; I strongly recommend getting in the habit of attempting them before moving on to the next section, as they reinforce the material we’ve just covered and will give you essential practice in using the many commands discussed.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; It’s not generally the case that they are &lt;em&gt;required&lt;/em&gt; to proceed, though, so if you get stuck it’s sometimes a good idea to continue forward and then revisit the exercise at a later time.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Indeed, this is good advice for the main text as well—you’ll be surprised how often a seemingly impossible idea or intractable problem will look easy the second time around.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A; &lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;By referring to &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-anatomy" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, identify the prompt, command, options, arguments, and cursor in each line of &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-command_exercise" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;6&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-terminal_tabs"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Most modern terminal programs have the ability to create multiple &lt;em&gt;tabs&lt;/em&gt; (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-terminal_tabs" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;7&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), which are useful for organizing a set of related terminal windows.&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-5" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-5"&gt;5&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; By examining the menu items for your terminal program (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-terminal_menu" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;8&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), figure out how to create a new tab.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Extra credit&lt;/em&gt;: Learn the keyboard shortcut for creating a new tab.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (Learning keyboard shortcuts for your system is an excellent habit to cultivate.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-new_tab"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-command_exercise" data-tralics-id="uid22" data-number="6"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/command_exercise.png" alt="images/figures/command_exercise"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 6: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;A series of typical commands.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-terminal_tabs" data-tralics-id="uid23" data-number="7"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/terminal_tabs.png" alt="images/figures/terminal_tabs"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 7: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;A terminal window with three tabs.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-terminal_menu" data-tralics-id="uid24" data-number="8"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/terminal_menu.png" alt="images/figures/terminal_menu"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 8: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Some menu items for the default macOS terminal.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-our_first_command" data-tralics-id="uid25" class="subsection" data-number="1.2"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-our_first_command" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;1.2 &lt;/span&gt;Our first command&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;We are now prepared to run our first command, which prints the word “hello” to the screen.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (The place where characters get printed is known as “standard out”, which is usually just the screen, and rarely refers to a physical printer.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The command is &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt;, and the argument is the string of characters—or simply &lt;em&gt;string&lt;/em&gt; for short—that we want to print.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To run the &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; command, type “echo hello” at the prompt, and then press the Return key (also called Enter):&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt; hello&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;hello&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;(I recommend always typing the commands out yourself, which will let you learn more than if you rely on copying and pasting.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Here we see that &lt;code&gt;echo hello&lt;/code&gt; prints “hello” and then returns another prompt.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Note that, for brevity, I’ve omitted all characters in the prompt except the dollar sign &lt;code&gt;$&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Just to make the pattern clear, let’s try a second &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; command:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="s2"&gt;"goodbye"&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;goodbye&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="s1"&gt;&#x0027;goodbye&#x0027;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;goodbye&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Note here that we’ve wrapped “goodbye” in quotation marks—and we also see that we can use either double quotes, as in &lt;code&gt;"goodbye"&lt;/code&gt;, or single quotes, as in &lt;code&gt;’goodbye’&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Such quotes can be used to group strings visually, though in many contexts they are not required by &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-hello_goodbye" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-6" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-6"&gt;6&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-hello_goodbye" data-tralics-id="uid27" data-number="1"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 1:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Printing “hello, goodbye” two different ways.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt; hello, goodbye&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;hello, goodbye&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="s2"&gt;"hello, goodbye"&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;hello, goodbye&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;One thing that can happen when using quotes is accidentally not matching them, as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="s2"&gt;"hello, goodbye&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;&amp;gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="s2"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;At this point, it seems we’re stuck.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; There are specific ways out of this quandary (in fact, in this case you can just add a closing quote and hit return), but it’s good to have a general strategy for getting out of trouble (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-cat_in_box" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;9&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-7" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-7"&gt;7&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This strategy is called “Ctrl-C” (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-getting_out_of_trouble" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-cat_in_box" data-tralics-id="uid29" data-number="9"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/cat_in_box.png" alt="images/figures/cat_in_box"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 9: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;This cat appears to be stuck and should probably hit &lt;code&gt;Ctrl-C&lt;/code&gt;.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="aside" id="aside-getting_out_of_trouble" data-tralics-id="uid30" data-number="4"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Box 4.&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Getting out of trouble&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;When using the command line, there are lots of things that can get you in trouble, by which I mean the terminal will just hang or otherwise end up in a state that makes entering further commands difficult or impossible.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Here are some examples of such commands:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ echo "hello&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ grep foobar&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ yes&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ tail&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ cat&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;In every case, the solution is the same: hit &lt;code class="tt"&gt;Ctrl-C&lt;/code&gt; (pronounced “control-see”).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Here &lt;code class="tt"&gt;Ctrl&lt;/code&gt; refers to the “control” key on your keyboard, and &lt;code class="tt"&gt;C&lt;/code&gt; refers to the key labeled “C”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;code class="tt"&gt;Ctrl-C&lt;/code&gt; thus means “While holding down the control key, press C.”&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In particular, &lt;code class="tt"&gt;C&lt;/code&gt; does &lt;em&gt;not&lt;/em&gt; refer to the capital letter C, so you should not press Shift in addition to Ctrl.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (&lt;code class="tt"&gt;Ctrl-C&lt;/code&gt; sends a &lt;em&gt;control code&lt;/em&gt; to the terminal and has nothing to do with producing a capital C when typing normal text.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The result of typing &lt;code class="tt"&gt;Ctrl-C&lt;/code&gt; is sometimes written as &lt;code class="inline_verbatim"&gt;⌃C&lt;/code&gt;, like this:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ tail&#x000A; ^C&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control-C" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;origins of &lt;code class="tt"&gt;Ctrl-C&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/a&gt; are somewhat obscure, but as a mnemonic I like to think of it as meaning “cancel”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; However you remember it, &lt;em&gt;do&lt;/em&gt; remember it: when you get into trouble at the command line, your best bet is usually to hit &lt;code class="tt"&gt;Ctrl-C&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Note&lt;/em&gt;: When &lt;code class="tt"&gt;Ctrl-C&lt;/code&gt; fails, 90% of the time hitting &lt;code class="tt"&gt;ESC&lt;/code&gt; (escape) will do the trick.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_first_command" data-tralics-id="uid31" class="subsubsection" data-number="1.2.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_first_command" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Write a command that prints out the string “hello, world”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Extra credit&lt;/em&gt;: As in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-hello_goodbye" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, do it two different ways, both with and without using quotation marks. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-hello-world"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Type the command &lt;code&gt;echo ’hello&lt;/code&gt; (with a mismatched single quote), and then get out of trouble using the technique from &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-getting_out_of_trouble" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-echo-hello"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-man_pages" data-tralics-id="uid34" class="subsection" data-number="1.3"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-man_pages" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;1.3 &lt;/span&gt;Man pages&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The program we’re using to run a command line, which is technically known as a &lt;em&gt;shell&lt;/em&gt;,&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-8" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-8"&gt;8&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; includes a powerful (though often cryptic) tool to learn more about available commands.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This tool is itself a command-line command called &lt;code&gt;man&lt;/code&gt; (short for “manual”).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Its argument is the name of the command (such as &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt;) that we want to learn more about.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The details are system-dependent, but on my system the result of running &lt;code&gt;man echo&lt;/code&gt; appears as in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-man_echo" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-man_echo" data-tralics-id="uid36" data-number="2"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 2:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;The result of running &lt;code&gt;man echo&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; man &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;ECHO(1)          BSD General Commands Manual         ECHO(1)&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;NAME&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;   echo -- write arguments to the standard output&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;SYNOPSIS&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;   echo [-n] [string ...]&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;DESCRIPTION&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;   The echo utility writes any specified operands, separated by single blank&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;   (` &#x0027;) characters and followed by a newline (`\n&#x0027;) character, to the stan-&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;   dard output.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;   The following option is available:&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;   -n  Do not print the trailing newline character. This may also be&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;      achieved by appending `\c&#x0027; to the end of the string, as is done by&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;      iBCS2 compatible systems. Note that this option as well as the&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;      effect of `\c&#x0027; are implementation-defined in IEEE Std 1003.1-2001&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;      (``POSIX.1&#x0027;&#x0027;) as amended by Cor. 1-2002. Applications aiming for&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;      maximum portability are strongly encouraged to use printf(1) to&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;      suppress the newline character.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="hll"&gt;&lt;span class="go"&gt;:                                                                             &lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;On the last line of &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-man_echo" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, note the presence of a colon &lt;code&gt;:&lt;/code&gt;, which indicates that there is more information below.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The details of this last line are system-dependent, but on any system you should be able to access subsequent information one line at a time by pressing the down arrow key, or one page at a time by pressing the spacebar.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To exit the man page, press “q” (for “quit”).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (This interface to the man pages is the same as for the &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt; program, which we’ll learn about in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-less_is_more" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3.3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-man_to_man" data-tralics-id="uid37" data-number="10"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/man_to_man.jpg" alt="images/figures/man_to_man"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 10: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Applying &lt;code&gt;man&lt;/code&gt; to &lt;code&gt;man&lt;/code&gt;.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Because &lt;code&gt;man&lt;/code&gt; itself is a command, we can apply &lt;code&gt;man&lt;/code&gt; to &lt;code&gt;man&lt;/code&gt; (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-man_to_man" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;10&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;),&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-9" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-9"&gt;9&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; as shown in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-man_man" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-man_man" data-tralics-id="uid39" data-number="3"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 3:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;The result of running &lt;code&gt;man man&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; man man&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;man(1)                                 man(1)&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;NAME&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;    man - format and display the on-line manual pages&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;SYNOPSIS&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;    man [-acdfFhkKtwW] [--path] [-m system] [-p string] [-C config_file]&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;    [-M pathlist] [-P pager] [-B browser] [-H htmlpager] [-S section_list]&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;    [section] name ...&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;DESCRIPTION&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;    man formats and displays the on-line manual pages. If you specify sec-&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;    tion, man only looks in that section of the manual. name is normally&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;    the name of the manual page, which is typically the name of a command,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;    function, or file. However, if name contains a slash (/) then man&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;    interprets it as a file specification, so that you can do man ./foo.5&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;    or even man /cd/foo/bar.1.gz.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;    See below for a description of where man looks for the manual page&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;    files.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;OPTIONS&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;    -C config_file&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;:&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;We can see from &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-man_man" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; that the synopsis of &lt;code&gt;man&lt;/code&gt; looks something like this:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;man [-acdfFhkKtwW] [--path] [-m system] [-p string] ...&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;This is what I meant above when I described man pages as “often cryptic”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Indeed, in many cases I find the details of man pages to be almost impossible to understand, but being able to scan over the man page to get a high-level overview of a command is a valuable skill, one worth acquiring.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To get used to reading man pages, I recommend running &lt;code&gt;man &amp;lt;command name&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt; when encountering a new command.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Even if the details aren’t entirely clear, reading the man pages will help develop the valuable skill of &lt;em&gt;technical sophistication&lt;/em&gt; (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-technical_sophistication" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-10" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-10"&gt;10&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="aside" id="aside-technical_sophistication" data-tralics-id="uid41" data-number="5"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Box 5.&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Technical sophistication&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;In mathematics, many subjects can be developed by applying pure deduction to a small number of assumptions, or &lt;em&gt;axioms&lt;/em&gt;; examples include algebra, geometry, number theory, and analysis.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As a result, such subjects are completely self-contained, and thus have no formal prerequisites—in principle, even a small child could learn them.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In practice, though, something else is required, and mathematicians often recommend the informal prerequisite of &lt;em&gt;mathematical maturity&lt;/em&gt;, which consists of the experience and general sophistication needed to understand and write mathematical proofs.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;In technology, a similar skill (or, more accurately, set of skills) exists in the form of &lt;em&gt;technical sophistication&lt;/em&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In addition to “hard skills” like familiarity with text editors and the Unix command line, technical sophistication includes “soft skills” like looking for promising menu items and knowing the kinds of search terms to drop into Google (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-tech_support_cheat_sheet" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;11&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), along with an &lt;em&gt;attitude&lt;/em&gt; of doing what it takes to make the machine do our bidding (&lt;a href="#aside-computer_magic" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; These soft skills, and this attitude, are hard to teach directly, so as you progress through this and subsequent &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough tutorials&lt;/a&gt; you should always be on the lookout for opportunities to increase your technical sophistication (such as, for example, learning how to get the gist of a program by scanning its man page (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-man_pages" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1.3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;)).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Over time, the cumulative effect will be that, like the author of &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-tech_support_cheat_sheet" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;11&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, you’ll have the seemingly magical ability to do everything in every program.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;By the way, &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-tech_support_cheat_sheet" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;11&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; is missing three important techniques for solving common problems:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Have you restarted the application?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Have you rebooted the device?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Have you tried uninstalling and reinstalling the app?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;#2 alone probably solves 90% of unexplained computer errors.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-tech_support_cheat_sheet" data-tralics-id="uid45" data-number="11"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/tech_support_cheat_sheet.png" alt="images/figures/tech_support_cheat_sheet"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 11: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;“&lt;a href="https://m.xkcd.com/627/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Tech Support Cheat Sheet&lt;/a&gt;” (via &lt;a href="http://xkcd.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;xkcd&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; See &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-technical_sophistication" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; for three extra techniques.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_man" data-tralics-id="uid46" class="subsubsection" data-number="1.3.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_man" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;According to the man page, what are the official short and long descriptions of &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; on your system? &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-man-echo"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;As seen in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-hello_goodbye" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, by default the &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; command prints its argument to the screen and then puts the new prompt on a new line.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The way it does this is by appending a special character called a &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newline" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;newline&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt; (a special character that literally puts the string on a new line, written in many contexts as “backslash n” &lt;code class="inline_verbatim"&gt;\n&lt;/code&gt;).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Because &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; is often used in programs to print out a sequence of strings &lt;em&gt;not&lt;/em&gt; separated by newlines, there is a special command-line option to prevent the newline from being inserted.&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;By reading the man page for &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt;, determine the command needed to print out “hello” &lt;em&gt;without&lt;/em&gt; the trailing newline, and verify using your terminal that it works as expected.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hints&lt;/em&gt;: To determine the placement of the command-line option, it may help to refer to &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-anatomy" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; By comparing your result with &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-with_newline" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-without_newline" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, you should be able to verify that you’ve used the option properly.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (&lt;em&gt;Note&lt;/em&gt;: This exercise may fail when using the default terminal program on some older versions of macOS.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In this case, I recommend installing &lt;a href="https://www.iterm2.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;iTerm&lt;/a&gt; (which isn’t a bad idea anyway).) &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-man-echo-hello"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-with_newline" data-tralics-id="uid49" data-number="4"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 4:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;The result of running &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; with a newline (without option).&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="go"&gt;hello&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;[~]$&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-without_newline" data-tralics-id="uid50" data-number="5"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 5:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;The result of running &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; without a newline (&lt;em&gt;with&lt;/em&gt; option).&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="go"&gt;hello[~]$&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-editing_the_line" data-tralics-id="uid51" class="subsection" data-number="1.4"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-editing_the_line" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;1.4 &lt;/span&gt;Editing the line&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Command lines include several features to make it easy to repeat previous commands, possibly in edited form.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; These and many other command-line features often involve special keys on the keyboard, so for reference &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#table-keyboard_symbols" class="hyperref"&gt;Table &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; shows these symbols for the various keys on a typical Macintosh keyboard.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Apply your technical sophistication (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-technical_sophistication" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) if your keyboard differs.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="table-keyboard_symbols" data-tralics-id="uid52" data-number="1" class="table"&gt;&lt;table class="tabular"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr class="bottom_border"&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Key&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Symbol&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Command&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;⌘&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Control&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;⌃&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Shift&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;⇧&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Option&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;⌥&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Up, down, left, right&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;↑ ↓ ← →&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Enter/Return&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;↵&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Tab&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;⇥&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Delete&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;⌫&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Table 1: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Miscellaneous keyboard symbols.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;One of the most useful ways to edit the line is to “up arrow” ↑, which simply retrieves the previous command.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Pressing up arrow again moves further up the list of commands, while “down arrow” ↓ goes back toward the bottom.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Other common ways to edit the line use the control key, which (as we saw in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-getting_out_of_trouble" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) is usually written as &lt;code&gt;Ctrl&lt;/code&gt; or &lt;code&gt;⌃&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For example, when typing a new command, or dealing with a previous command, it is often convenient to be able to move quickly within the line.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Suppose we typed&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; goodbye&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;only to realize that we wanted to put &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; in front of it.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; We could use the left arrow key ← to get to the beginning of the line, but it’s easier to type &lt;code&gt;⌃A&lt;/code&gt;, which takes us there immediately.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Similarly, &lt;code&gt;⌃E&lt;/code&gt; moves to the end of the line.&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-11" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-11"&gt;11&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Finally, &lt;code&gt;⌃U&lt;/code&gt; clears to the beginning of the line and lets us start over.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The combination of &lt;code&gt;⌃A&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;⌃E&lt;/code&gt;, and &lt;code&gt;⌃U&lt;/code&gt; will work on most systems, but they don’t do you much good if you’re editing a longer line, such as this one containing the first line of &lt;a href="http://www.shakespeares-sonnets.com/sonnet/1" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Sonnet 1 by William Shakespeare&lt;/a&gt; (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-sonnet_1" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;6&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-sonnet_1" data-tralics-id="uid54" data-number="6"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 6:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Printing the first line of Shakespeare’s first sonnet.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="s2"&gt;"From fairest creatures we desire increase,"&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;Suppose we wanted to change “From” to “FRom” to more closely match the text from the original sonnet (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-sonnet_1" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;12&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-12" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-12"&gt;12&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; We could type &lt;code&gt;⌃A&lt;/code&gt; followed by the right arrow key a few times, but on some systems it’s possible to move directly to the desired spot by combining the keyboard and mouse via Option-click.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; That is, you can hold down the Option key on your keyboard (if it exists),&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-13" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-13"&gt;13&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; and then click with the mouse pointer on the place in the command where you want the cursor.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This would let us move right to the “o” in “From”, allowing us to delete the “r” and yielding &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-sonnet_1_edited" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;7&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; directly.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-sonnet_1" data-tralics-id="uid57" data-number="12"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/Sonnet_1.jpg" alt="images/figures/Sonnet_1"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 12: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;The original appearance of Shakespeare’s first sonnet.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-sonnet_1_edited" data-tralics-id="uid58" data-number="7"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 7:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;The result of editing a longer command-line command.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="s2"&gt;"FRom fairest creatures we desire increase,"&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;I usually move around the command line with a combination of &lt;code&gt;⌃A&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;⌃E&lt;/code&gt;, and right &amp;amp; left arrow keys, but for longer commands Option-click can be a big help.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (I also frequently change my mind about the exact command I’m typing, in which case I usually find that hitting &lt;code&gt;⌃U&lt;/code&gt; and starting over again is the fastest way to proceed.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_editing_the_line" data-tralics-id="uid59" class="subsubsection" data-number="1.4.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_editing_the_line" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Using the up arrow, print to the screen the strings “fee”, “fie”, “foe”, and “fum” without retyping &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; each time. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-up-arrow"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Starting with the line in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-sonnet_1" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;6&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, use any combination of &lt;code&gt;⌃A&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;⌃E&lt;/code&gt;, arrow keys, or Option-click to change the occurrences of the short s to the archaic &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Long_s" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;long s&lt;/a&gt; “ſ” in order to match the appearance of the original (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-sonnet_1" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;12&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In other words, the argument to &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; should read “FRom faireſt creatures we deſire increaſe,”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: It’s unlikely that your keyboard can produce “ſ” natively, so either copy it from the text of this tutorial or &lt;a href="http://lmgtfy.com/?q=unicode+long+s" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Google for it&lt;/a&gt; and copy it from the Internet.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (If you have trouble copying and pasting into your terminal, I suggest applying the ideas in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-technical_sophistication" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to figure out how to do it on your system.) &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-archaic"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-cleaning_up" data-tralics-id="uid62" class="subsection" data-number="1.5"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-cleaning_up" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;1.5 &lt;/span&gt;Cleaning up&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;When using the command line, sometimes it’s convenient to be able to clean up by clearing the screen, which we can do with &lt;code&gt;clear&lt;/code&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; clear&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;A keyboard shortcut for this is &lt;code&gt;⌃L&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Similarly, when we are done with a terminal window (or tab) and are ready to exit, we can use the &lt;code&gt;exit&lt;/code&gt; command:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;exit&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;A keyboard shortcut for this is &lt;code&gt;⌃D&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_cleaning" data-tralics-id="uid63" class="subsubsection" data-number="1.5.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_cleaning" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Clear the contents of the current tab. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-clear-contents"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Open a new tab, execute &lt;code&gt;echo ’hello’&lt;/code&gt;, and then exit. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-new-tab"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-summary_cleaning" data-tralics-id="uid66" class="subsection" data-number="1.6"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-summary_cleaning" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;1.6 &lt;/span&gt;Summary&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Important commands from this section are summarized in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#table-man_echo" class="hyperref"&gt;Table &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="table-man_echo" data-tralics-id="uid67" data-number="2" class="table"&gt;&lt;table class="tabular"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr class="bottom_border"&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Command&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Description&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Example&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;echo &amp;lt;string&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Print string to screen&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ echo hello&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;man &amp;lt;command&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Display manual page for command&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ man echo&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;⌃C&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Get out of trouble&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ tail&lt;/code&gt;&lt;code class="inline_verbatim"&gt;^C&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;⌃A&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Move to beginning of line&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;⌃E&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Move to end of line&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;⌃U&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Delete to beginning of line&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Option-click&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Move cursor to location clicked&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Up &amp;amp; down arrow&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Scroll through previous commands&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;clear&lt;/code&gt; or &lt;code class="tt"&gt;⌃L&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Clear screen&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ clear&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;exit&lt;/code&gt; or &lt;code class="tt"&gt;⌃D&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Exit terminal&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ exit&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Table 2: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Important commands from &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-basics" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_summary_basics" data-tralics-id="uid68" class="subsubsection" data-number="1.6.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_summary_basics" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Write a command to print the string &lt;code&gt;Use "man echo"&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;em&gt;including&lt;/em&gt; the quotes; i.e., take care not to print out &lt;code&gt;Use man echo&lt;/code&gt; instead.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: Use double quotes in the inner string, and wrap the whole thing in single quotes. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-command-man"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;By running &lt;code&gt;man sleep&lt;/code&gt;, figure out how to make the terminal “sleep” for 5 seconds, and execute the command to do so. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-man-sleep"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Execute the command to sleep for 5000 seconds, realize that’s well over an hour, and then use the instructions from &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-getting_out_of_trouble" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to get out of trouble. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-out-of-trouble"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="sec-manipulating_files" data-tralics-id="cid2" class="section" data-number="2"&gt;&lt;h2&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-manipulating_files" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;2 &lt;/span&gt;Manipulating files&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Having covered how to run a basic command, we’re now ready to learn how to manipulate files, one of the most important tasks at the command line.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Because this tutorial assumes no technical prerequisites, we’re not going to require any familiarity with programs designed to edit text.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (Such programs, called &lt;em&gt;text editors&lt;/em&gt;, are the subject of the next tutorial in the sequence, &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/text-editor-tutorial" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Learn Enough Text Editor to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This means that we’ll need to create files by hand at the command line.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; But this is a feature, not a bug (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-speak_geek" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;6&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), because learning to create files at the command line is a valuable skill in itself.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="aside" id="aside-speak_geek" data-tralics-id="uid72" data-number="6"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Box 6.&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Learning to speak “geek”&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;One important part of learning software development is becoming familiar with the &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/~esr/faqs/hacker-howto.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;hacker&lt;/a&gt;, nerd, and geek culture from which much of it springs.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For example, the phrase “It’s not a bug, it’s a feature” is a common way of recasting a seeming flaw as a virtue.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As the Urban Dictionary &lt;a href="http://www.urbandictionary.com/define.php?term=It%27s+not+a+bug%2C+it%27s+a+feature&amp;amp;defid=6751775" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;puts it&lt;/a&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;blockquote class="quotation"&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;It’s not a bug, it’s a feature&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Excuse made by software developers when they try to convince the user that a flaw in their program is actually what it’s supposed to be doing.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;The &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Jargon File&lt;/a&gt;, which includes an &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/go01.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;enormous and entertaining lexicon&lt;/a&gt; of hacker terms, expands on this theme in its entry on &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/F/feature.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;feature&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;blockquote class="quotation"&gt;&lt;p&gt;“Undocumented feature” is a common, allegedly humorous euphemism for a &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/B/bug.html" target="_blank"
