rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;bug&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; There’s a related joke that is sometimes referred to as the “one-question geek test”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; You say to someone “I saw a Volkswagen Beetle today with a vanity license plate that read FEATURE”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; If he/she laughs, he/she is a &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/G/geek.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;geek&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;The joke here is that, because “bug” is a common slang term for a Volkswagen Beetle, a Beetle with the vanity plate FEATURE is a real-life manifestation of “It’s not a bug, it’s a feature” (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-bug_feature" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;13&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Even if you’re not a geek or nerd yourself, learning to “speak geek” will help you navigate both the technological landscape and the social world that surrounds it.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-bug_feature" data-tralics-id="uid73" data-number="13"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/bug_feature.png" alt="images/figures/bug_feature"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 13: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;It’s not a bug, it’s a feature.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-redirecting_and_appending" data-tralics-id="uid74" class="subsection" data-number="2.1"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-redirecting_and_appending" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;2.1 &lt;/span&gt;Redirecting and appending&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Let’s pick up (more or less) where we left off in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-basics" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, with an &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; command to print out the first line of Shakespeare’s first sonnet (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-sonnet_1" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;6&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;):&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="s2"&gt;"From fairest creatures we desire increase,"&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;From fairest creatures we desire increase,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Our task now is to create a file containing this line.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Even without the benefit of a text editor, it is possible to do this using the &lt;em&gt;redirect operator&lt;/em&gt; &lt;code&gt;&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="s2"&gt;"From fairest creatures we desire increase,"&lt;/span&gt; &amp;gt; sonnet_1.txt&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;(Recall that you can use up arrow to retrieve the previous command rather than typing it from scratch.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Here the right angle bracket &lt;code&gt;&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt; takes the string output from &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; and redirects its contents to a file called &lt;code&gt;sonnet_1.txt&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;How can we tell if the redirect worked?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; We’ll learn some more advanced command-line tools for inspecting files in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-inspecting_files" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, but for now we’ll use the &lt;code&gt;cat&lt;/code&gt; command, which simply dumps the contents of the file to the screen:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; cat sonnet_1.txt&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;From fairest creatures we desire increase,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The name &lt;code&gt;cat&lt;/code&gt; is short for “&lt;a href="http://dictionary.reference.com/browse/concatenate" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;concatenate&lt;/a&gt;”, which is a hint that it can be used to combine the contents of multiple files, but the usage above (to dump the contents of a single file to the screen) is extremely common.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Think of &lt;code&gt;cat&lt;/code&gt; as a “quick-and-dirty” way to view the contents of a particular file (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-cat" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;14&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-14" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-14"&gt;14&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-cat" data-tralics-id="uid76" data-number="14"&gt;&lt;span class="graphics"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/cat.jpg" alt="cat"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 14: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Viewing a file with &lt;code&gt;cat&lt;/code&gt;.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;In order to add the second line of the sonnet (in modernized spelling), we can use the &lt;em&gt;append operator&lt;/em&gt; &lt;code&gt;&amp;gt;&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt; as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="s2"&gt;"That thereby beauty&#x0027;s Rose might never die,"&lt;/span&gt; &amp;gt;&amp;gt; sonnet_1.txt&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;This just adds the line to the end of the given file.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As before, we can see the result using &lt;code&gt;cat&lt;/code&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; cat sonnet_1.txt&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;From fairest creatures we desire increase,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;That thereby beauty&#x0027;s Rose might never die,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;(To get to this command, I hope you just hit up arrow twice instead of retyping it.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; If so, you’re definitely getting the hang of this.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The result above shows that the double right angle bracket &lt;code&gt;&amp;gt;&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt; appended the string from &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; to the file &lt;code&gt;sonnet_1.txt&lt;/code&gt; as expected.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Modernized treatments of the &lt;em&gt;Sonnets&lt;/em&gt; sometimes &lt;a href="http://dictionary.reference.com/browse/emend" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;emend&lt;/a&gt; &lt;em&gt;Rose&lt;/em&gt; to &lt;em&gt;rose&lt;/em&gt; (thereby obscuring the &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tudor_rose" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;likely meaning&lt;/a&gt;), and we can make a second file following this convention using two more calls to &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="s2"&gt;"From fairest creatures we desire increase,"&lt;/span&gt; &amp;gt; sonnet_1_lower_case.txt&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="s2"&gt;"That thereby beauty&#x0027;s rose might never die,"&lt;/span&gt; &amp;gt;&amp;gt; sonnet_1_lower_case.txt&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;In order to facilitate the comparison of files that are similar but not identical, Unix systems come with the helpful &lt;code&gt;diff&lt;/code&gt; command:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;$ diff sonnet_1.txt sonnet_1_lower_case.txt&#x000A;&amp;lt; That thereby beauty&#x0027;s Rose might never die,&#x000A;&lt;span class="gd"&gt;---&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&amp;gt; That thereby beauty&#x0027;s rose might never die,&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;When discussing computer files, &lt;em&gt;diff&lt;/em&gt; is frequently employed both as a noun (“What’s the diff between those files?”) and as a verb (“You should diff the files to see what changed.”).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As with many technical terms, this sometimes bleeds over into common usage, such as “Diff present ideas against those of various past cultures, and see what you get.”&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-15" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-15"&gt;15&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_redirecting_appending" data-tralics-id="uid78" class="subsubsection" data-number="2.1.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_redirecting_appending" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;At the end of each of the exercises below, use the &lt;code&gt;cat&lt;/code&gt; command to verify your answer.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A; &lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Using &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;, make files called &lt;code&gt;line_1.txt&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;line_2.txt&lt;/code&gt; containing the first and second lines of Sonnet 1, respectively. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-echo-redirect"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Replicate the original &lt;code&gt;sonnet_1.txt&lt;/code&gt; (containing the first two lines of the sonnet) by first redirecting the contents of &lt;code&gt;line_1.txt&lt;/code&gt; and then appending the contents of &lt;code&gt;line_2.txt&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Call the new file &lt;code&gt;sonnet_1_copy.txt&lt;/code&gt;, and confirm using &lt;code&gt;diff&lt;/code&gt; that it’s identical to &lt;code&gt;sonnet_1.txt&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: When there is no diff between two files, &lt;code&gt;diff&lt;/code&gt; simply outputs nothing. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-echo-redirect-append"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Use &lt;code&gt;cat&lt;/code&gt; to combine the contents of &lt;code&gt;line_1.txt&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;line_2.txt&lt;/code&gt; in reverse order using a &lt;em&gt;single&lt;/em&gt; command, yielding the file &lt;code&gt;sonnet_1_reversed.txt&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: The &lt;code&gt;cat&lt;/code&gt; command can take multiple arguments. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-echo-redirect-reverse"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-listing" data-tralics-id="uid82" class="subsection" data-number="2.2"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-listing" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;2.2 &lt;/span&gt;Listing&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Perhaps the mostly frequently typed command on the Unix command line is &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt;, short for “list” (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-ls" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;8&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-ls" data-tralics-id="uid83" data-number="8"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 8:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Listing files and directories with &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (Output will vary.)&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Desktop&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Downloads&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;sonnet_1.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;sonnet_1_reversed.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;The &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; command simply lists all the files and directories in the current directory (except for those that are &lt;em&gt;hidden&lt;/em&gt;, which we’ll learn more about in a moment).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In this sense, it’s effectively a command-line version of the graphical browser used to show files and directories (also called “folders”), as seen in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-file_listing" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;15&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (We’ll sharpen our understanding of directories and folders in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-directories" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As with a graphical file browser, the output in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-ls" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;8&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; is just a sample, and results will differ based on the details of your system.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (This goes for all the &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; examples, so don’t be concerned if there are minor differences in output.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-file_listing" data-tralics-id="uid84" data-number="15"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/file_listing.png" alt="images/figures/file_listing"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 15: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;The graphical equivalent of &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt;.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; command can be used to check if a file (or directory) exists, because trying to &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; a nonexistent file results in an error message, as seen in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-ls_no_such" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;9&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-ls_no_such" data-tralics-id="uid85" data-number="9"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 9:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Running &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; on a nonexistent file.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls foo&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;ls: foo: No such file or directory&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; touch foo&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls foo&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;foo&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-ls_no_such" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;9&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; uses the &lt;code&gt;touch&lt;/code&gt; command to create an empty file with the name &lt;code&gt;foo&lt;/code&gt; (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-foo_bar" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;7&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), so the second time we run &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; the error message is gone.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (The stated purpose of &lt;code&gt;touch&lt;/code&gt; is to change the modification time on files or directories, but (ab)using &lt;code&gt;touch&lt;/code&gt; to create empty files as in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-ls_no_such" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;9&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; is a common Unix idiom.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="aside" id="aside-foo_bar" data-tralics-id="uid86" data-number="7"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Box 7.&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Foo, bar, baz, etc.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;When reading about computers, you will encounter certain strange words—words like &lt;em&gt;foo&lt;/em&gt;, &lt;em&gt;bar&lt;/em&gt;, and &lt;em&gt;baz&lt;/em&gt;—with surprising frequency.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Indeed, in addition to &lt;code class="tt"&gt;ls foo&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code class="tt"&gt;touch foo&lt;/code&gt;, we have already seen four such references in this tutorial: in a typical command-line command (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-command_line_command" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), in a virtual machine password (&lt;code class="tt"&gt;foobar!&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-virtual_machine" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), again when getting out of trouble (&lt;code class="tt"&gt;grep foobar&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-getting_out_of_trouble" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), and yet again in a man page (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-man_man" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The first three were my own uses, but the last I had nothing to do with:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; ...if name contains a slash (/) then man interprets&#x000A; it as a file specification,  so that you can do man&#x000A; ./foo.5 or even man /cd/foo/bar.1.gz.&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Here we see both &lt;em&gt;foo&lt;/em&gt; and &lt;em&gt;bar&lt;/em&gt; making an appearance in the man page for &lt;code class="tt"&gt;man&lt;/code&gt; itself—an unambiguous testament to their ubiquity in computing.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;What is the origin of these odd terms?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As usual, the &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Jargon File&lt;/a&gt; (via its entry on &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/F/foo.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;foo&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) enlightens us:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;blockquote class="quotation"&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;foo&lt;/strong&gt;: /foo/&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;1.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; interj.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Term of disgust.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;2.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; [very common] Used very generally as a sample name for absolutely anything, esp. programs and files (esp. scratch files).&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;3.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; First on the standard list of &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/M/metasyntactic-variable.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;metasyntactic variable&lt;/a&gt;s used in syntax examples.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; See also &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/B/bar.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;bar&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/B/baz.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;baz&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/Q/qux.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;qux&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/Q/quux.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;quux&lt;/a&gt;, etc.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;When ‘foo’ is used in connection with ‘bar’ it has generally traced to the WWII-era Army slang acronym &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/F/FUBAR.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;FUBAR&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt; [&lt;a href="http://www.urbandictionary.com/define.php?term=fubar" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;see original meaning&lt;/a&gt;], later modified to &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/F/foobar.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;foobar&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Early versions of the Jargon File interpreted this change as a post-war bowdlerization, but it now seems more likely that FUBAR was itself a derivative of ‘foo’ perhaps influenced by German &lt;em&gt;furchtbar&lt;/em&gt; (terrible) — ‘foobar’ may actually have been the &lt;em&gt;original&lt;/em&gt; form.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Following the link to &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/M/metasyntactic-variable.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;metasyntactic variable&lt;/a&gt;s, we then find the following:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;blockquote class="quotation"&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;metasyntactic variable&lt;/strong&gt;: n.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;A name used in examples and understood to stand for whatever thing is under discussion, or any random member of a class of things under discussion.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The word foo is the canonical example.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To avoid confusion, hackers never (well, hardly ever) use ‘foo’ or other words like it as permanent names for anything.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In filenames, a common convention is that any filename beginning with a metasyntactic-variable name is a scratch file that may be deleted at any time.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Metasyntactic variables are so called because (1) they are variables in the metalanguage used to talk about programs, etc.; (2) they are variables whose values are often variables (as in usages like “the value of f(foo,bar) is the sum of foo and bar”).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; However, it has been plausibly suggested that the real reason for the term “metasyntactic variable” is that it sounds good.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;In other words, if you want to create a file, and the name doesn’t matter, the name is usually “foo”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Once you’ve used “foo”, the next file is called “bar”, the one after that “baz”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Continuations from there vary (“quux” is one &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/Q/quux.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;common choice&lt;/a&gt;), but in many cases three is enough.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;A common pattern when using the command line is changing directories using &lt;code&gt;cd&lt;/code&gt; (covered in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-directories" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) and then immediately typing &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; to view the contents of the directory.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This lets us orient ourselves, and is a good first step toward whatever our next action might be.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;One useful ability of &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; is support for the &lt;em&gt;wildcard character&lt;/em&gt; &lt;code&gt;*&lt;/code&gt; (read “star”).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For example, to list all files ending in “.txt”, we would type this:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls *.txt&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;sonnet_1.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;sonnet_1_reversed.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Here &lt;code&gt;*.txt&lt;/code&gt; (read “star dot tee-ex-tee”) automatically expands to all the filenames that match the pattern “any string followed by .txt”.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;There are three particularly important optional forms of &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt;, starting with the “long form”, using the option &lt;code&gt;-l&lt;/code&gt; (read “dash-ell”):&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls -l *.txt&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;total 16&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;-rw-r--r-- 1 mhartl staff  87 Jul 20 18:05 sonnet_1.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;-rw-r--r-- 1 mhartl staff 294 Jul 21 12:09 sonnet_1_reversed.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;For now, you can safely ignore most of the information output by &lt;code&gt;ls -l&lt;/code&gt;, but note that the long form lists a date and time indicating the last time the file was modified.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The number before the date is the &lt;em&gt;size&lt;/em&gt; of the file, in bytes.&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-16" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-16"&gt;16&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;A second powerful &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; variant is “list by &lt;strong&gt;r&lt;/strong&gt;eversed &lt;strong&gt;t&lt;/strong&gt;ime of modification (&lt;strong&gt;l&lt;/strong&gt;ong format)”, or &lt;code&gt;ls -rtl&lt;/code&gt;, which lists the long form of each file or directory in order of how recently it was modified (&lt;em&gt;reversed&lt;/em&gt; so that the most recently modified entries appear at the bottom of the screen for easy inspection).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This is particularly useful when there are a lot of files in the directory but you really only care about seeing the ones that have been modified recently, such when confirming a file download.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; We’ll see an example of this in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-downloading_a_file" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3.1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, but you are free to try it now:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls -rtl&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;&amp;lt;results system-dependent&amp;gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;By the way, &lt;code&gt;-rtl&lt;/code&gt; is the commonly used compact form, but you can also pass the options individually, like this:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls -r -t -l&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;In addition, their order is irrelevant, so typing &lt;code&gt;ls -trl&lt;/code&gt; gives the same result.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-hidden_files" data-tralics-id="uid88" class="subsubsection" data-number="2.2.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-hidden_files" class="heading"&gt;Hidden files&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Finally, Unix has the concept of “hidden files (and directories)”, which don’t show up by default when listing files.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Hidden files and directories are identified by starting with a dot &lt;code&gt;.&lt;/code&gt;, and are commonly used for things like storing user preferences.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For example, in &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/git" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Learn Enough Git to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, we’ll create a file called &lt;code&gt;.gitignore&lt;/code&gt; that tells a particular program (Git) to ignore files matching certain patterns.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As a concrete example, to ignore all files ending in “.txt”, we could do this:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="s2"&gt;"*.txt"&lt;/span&gt; &amp;gt; .gitignore&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; cat .gitignore&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;*.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;If we then run &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt;, the file won’t show up, because it’s hidden:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;sonnet_1.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;sonnet_1_reversed.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;To get &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; to display hidden files and directories, we need to pass it the &lt;code&gt;-a&lt;/code&gt; option (for “all”):&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls -a&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;.           .gitignore      sonnet_1_reversed.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;..          sonnet_1.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Now &lt;code&gt;.gitignore&lt;/code&gt; shows up, as expected.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (We’ll learn what &lt;code&gt;.&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;..&lt;/code&gt; refer to in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-navigating_directories" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4.3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_listing" data-tralics-id="uid89" class="subsubsection" data-number="2.2.2"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_listing" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;What’s the command to list all the non-hidden files and directories that start with the letter “s”? &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-command-list-all-prefix"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;What is the command to list all the non-hidden files that contain the string “onnet”, long-form by reverse modification time?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: Use the wildcard operator at both the beginning and the end. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-command-list-all-contains"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;What is the command to list &lt;em&gt;all&lt;/em&gt; files (including hidden ones) by reverse modification time, in long form? &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-command-list-all-reverse-mod"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-renaming_copying_deleting" data-tralics-id="uid93" class="subsection" data-number="2.3"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-renaming_copying_deleting" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;2.3 &lt;/span&gt;Renaming, copying, deleting&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Next to listing files, probably the most common file operations involve renaming, copying, and deleting them.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As with listing files, most modern operating systems provide a graphical user interface to such tasks, but in many contexts it is more convenient to perform them at the command line.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The way to rename a file is with the &lt;code&gt;mv&lt;/code&gt; command, short for “move”:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="s2"&gt;"test text"&lt;/span&gt; &amp;gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;test&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="hll"&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; mv &lt;span class="nb"&gt;test&lt;/span&gt; test_file.txt&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;test_file.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;This renames the file called &lt;code&gt;test&lt;/code&gt; to &lt;code&gt;test_file.txt&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The final step in the example runs &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; to confirm that the file renaming was successful, but system-specific files other than the test file are omitted from the output shown.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (The name “move” comes from the general use of &lt;code&gt;mv&lt;/code&gt; to move a file to a different directory (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-directories" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), possibly renaming it en route.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; When the origin and target directories coincide, such a “move” reduces to a simple renaming.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The way to copy a file is with &lt;code&gt;cp&lt;/code&gt;, short for “copy”:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="hll"&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; cp test_file.txt second_test.txt&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;second_test.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;test_file.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Finally, the command for deleting a file is &lt;code&gt;rm&lt;/code&gt;, for “remove”:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="hll"&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; rm second_test.txt&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="go"&gt;remove second_test.txt? y&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls second_test.txt&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;ls: second_test.txt: No such file or directory&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Note that, on many systems, by default you will be prompted to confirm the removal of the file.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Any answer starting with the letter “y” or “Y” will cause the file to be deleted, and any other answers will prevent the deletion from occurring.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;By the way, in the calls to &lt;code&gt;cp&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;rm&lt;/code&gt; above, I would almost certainly not type out &lt;code&gt;test_file.txt&lt;/code&gt; or &lt;code&gt;second_test.txt&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Instead, I would type something like &lt;code&gt;test⇥&lt;/code&gt; or &lt;code&gt;sec⇥&lt;/code&gt; (where ⇥ represents the tab key (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#table-keyboard_symbols" class="hyperref"&gt;Table &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;)), thereby making use of &lt;em&gt;tab completion&lt;/em&gt; (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-tab_completion" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;8&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="aside" id="aside-tab_completion" data-tralics-id="uid94" data-number="8"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Box 8.&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Tab completion&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Most modern command-line programs (shells) support &lt;em&gt;tab completion&lt;/em&gt;, which involves automatically completing a word if there’s only one valid match on the system.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For example, if the only file starting with the letters “tes” is &lt;code class="tt"&gt;test_file&lt;/code&gt;, we could create the command to remove it as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ rm tes⇥&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;where ⇥ is the tab key (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#table-keyboard_symbols" class="hyperref"&gt;Table &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The shell would then complete the filename, yielding &lt;code class="tt"&gt;rm test_file&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Especially with longer filenames (or directories), tab completion can save a huge amount of typing.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; It also lowers the &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_load" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;cognitive load&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, since it means you don’t have to remember the full name of the file—only its first few letters.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;If the match is ambiguous, as would happen if we had files called &lt;code class="tt"&gt;foobarquux&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code class="tt"&gt;foobazquux&lt;/code&gt;, the word will be completed only as far as possible, so&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ ls foo⇥&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;would be completed to&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ ls fooba&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;If we then hit tab &lt;em&gt;again&lt;/em&gt;, we would see a list of matches:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ ls fooba⇥&#x000A; foobarquux foobazquux&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;We could then type more letters to resolve the ambiguity, so typing the &lt;code class="tt"&gt;r&lt;/code&gt; after &lt;code class="tt"&gt;fooba&lt;/code&gt; and hitting &lt;code class="tt"&gt;⇥&lt;/code&gt; would yield&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ ls foobar⇥&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;which would be completed to &lt;code class="tt"&gt;foobarquux&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This situation is common enough that experienced command-line users will often just hit something like &lt;code class="tt"&gt;f⇥⇥&lt;/code&gt; to get the shell to show all the possibilities:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ ls f⇥⇥&#x000A; figure_1.png foobarquux  foobazquux&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Additional letters would then be typed as usual to resolve the ambiguity.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;The default behavior of &lt;code&gt;rm&lt;/code&gt; on an unconfigured Unix system is actually to remove the file without confirmation, but (because deletion is irreversible) many systems &lt;em&gt;alias&lt;/em&gt; the &lt;code&gt;rm&lt;/code&gt; command to use an option to turn on confirmation.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (As you can verify by running &lt;code&gt;man rm&lt;/code&gt;, this option is &lt;code&gt;-i&lt;/code&gt;, so in fact &lt;code&gt;rm&lt;/code&gt; is really &lt;code&gt;rm -i&lt;/code&gt;.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; There are many situations where confirmation is inconvenient, though, such as when you’re deleting a list of files and don’t want to have to confirm each one.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This is especially common when using the wildcard &lt;code&gt;*&lt;/code&gt; introduced in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-listing" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2.2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For example, to remove all the files ending with “.txt” using a single command, &lt;em&gt;without&lt;/em&gt; having to confirm each one, you can type this:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; rm -f *.txt&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Here &lt;code&gt;-f&lt;/code&gt; (for “force”) overrides the implicit &lt;code&gt;-i&lt;/code&gt; option and removes all files immediately.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (&lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nota_bene" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;N.B.&lt;/a&gt; You are now in a position to understand the command in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-command_line_command" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-unix_terseness" data-tralics-id="uid95" class="subsubsection" data-number="2.3.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-unix_terseness" class="heading"&gt;Unix terseness&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;One thing you might notice is that the commands in this section and in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-listing" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2.2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; are short: instead of &lt;code&gt;list&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;move&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;copy&lt;/code&gt;, and &lt;code&gt;remove&lt;/code&gt;, we have &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;mv&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;cp&lt;/code&gt;, and &lt;code&gt;rm&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Because the former command names are easier to understand and memorize, you may wonder why the actual commands aren’t longer (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-y_u_no" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;16&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-y_u_no" data-tralics-id="uid96" data-number="16"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image box"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/y_u_no.jpg" alt="images/figures/y_u_no"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 16: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;The terseness of Unix commands can be a source of confusion.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The answer is that Unix dates from a time when most computer users logged on to centralized servers over slow connections, and there could be a noticeable delay between the time users pressed a key and the time it appeared on the terminal.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For frequently used commands like listing files, the difference between &lt;code&gt;list&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; or &lt;code&gt;remove&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;rm&lt;/code&gt; could be significant.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As a result, the most commonly used Unix commands tend to be only two or three letters long.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Because it makes them more difficult to memorize, this can be a minor inconvenience when learning them, but over a lifetime of command-line use the savings represented by, say, &lt;code&gt;mv&lt;/code&gt; really add up.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_manipulating" data-tralics-id="uid97" class="subsubsection" data-number="2.3.2"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_manipulating" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Use the &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; command and the redirect operator &lt;code&gt;&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt; to make a file called &lt;code&gt;foo.txt&lt;/code&gt; containing the text “hello, world”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Then, using the &lt;code&gt;cp&lt;/code&gt; command, make a copy of &lt;code&gt;foo.txt&lt;/code&gt; called &lt;code&gt;bar.txt&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Using the &lt;code&gt;diff&lt;/code&gt; command, confirm that the contents of both files are the same. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-echo-redirect-cp"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;By combining the &lt;code&gt;cat&lt;/code&gt; command and the redirect operator &lt;code&gt;&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;, create a copy of &lt;code&gt;foo.txt&lt;/code&gt; called &lt;code&gt;baz.txt&lt;/code&gt; &lt;em&gt;without&lt;/em&gt; using the &lt;code&gt;cp&lt;/code&gt; command. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-cat-redirect-cp"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Create a file called &lt;code&gt;quux.txt&lt;/code&gt; containing the contents of &lt;code&gt;foo.txt&lt;/code&gt; followed by the contents of &lt;code&gt;bar.txt&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: As noted in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-exercises_redirecting_appending" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2.1.1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;code&gt;cat&lt;/code&gt; can take multiple arguments. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-cat-combine"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;How do &lt;code&gt;rm nonexistent&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;rm -f nonexistent&lt;/code&gt; differ for a nonexistent file? &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-rm-f"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-summary_manipulating" data-tralics-id="uid102" class="subsection" data-number="2.4"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-summary_manipulating" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;2.4 &lt;/span&gt;Summary&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Important commands from this section are summarized in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#table-manipulating_files" class="hyperref"&gt;Table &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="table-manipulating_files" data-tralics-id="uid103" data-number="3" class="table"&gt;&lt;table class="tabular"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr class="bottom_border"&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Command&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Description&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Example&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Redirect output to filename&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ echo foo &amp;gt; foo.txt&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;&amp;gt;&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Append output to filename&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ echo bar &amp;gt;&amp;gt; foo.txt&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;cat &amp;lt;file&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Print contents of file to screen&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ cat hello.txt&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;diff &amp;lt;f1&amp;gt; &amp;lt;f2&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Diff files 1 &amp;amp; 2&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ diff foo.txt bar.txt&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;List directory or file&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ ls hello.txt&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;ls -l&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;List long form&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ ls -l hello.txt&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;ls -rtl&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Long by reverse modification time&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ ls -rtl&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;ls -a&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;List all (including hidden)&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ ls -a&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;touch &amp;lt;file&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Create an empty file&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ touch foo&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;mv &amp;lt;old&amp;gt; &amp;lt;new&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Rename (move) from old to new&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ mv foo bar&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;cp &amp;lt;old&amp;gt; &amp;lt;new&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Copy old to new&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ cp foo bar&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;rm &amp;lt;file&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Remove (delete) file&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ rm foo&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;rm -f &amp;lt;file&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Force-remove file&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ rm -f bar&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Table 3: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Important commands from &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-manipulating_files" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_summary_manipulating" data-tralics-id="uid104" class="subsubsection" data-number="2.4.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_summary_manipulating" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="fig-copy_paste_sonnet_1" data-tralics-id="uid105" data-number="17" class="figure"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;blockquote class="quotation"&gt;&lt;p&gt;FRom faireſt creatures we deſire increaſe, &lt;span class="break"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;That thereby beauties &lt;em&gt;Roſe&lt;/em&gt; might neuer die, &lt;span class="break"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;But as the riper ſhould by time deceaſe, &lt;span class="break"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;His tender heire might beare his memory: &lt;span class="break"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;But thou contracted to thine owne bright eyes, &lt;span class="break"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;Feed’ſt thy lights flame with ſelfe ſubſtantiall fewell, &lt;span class="break"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;Making a famine where aboundance lies, &lt;span class="break"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;Thy ſelfe thy foe,to thy ſweet ſelfe too cruell: &lt;span class="break"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;Thou that art now the worlds freſh ornament, &lt;span class="break"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;And only herauld to the gaudy ſpring, &lt;span class="break"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;Within thine owne bud burieſt thy content, &lt;span class="break"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;And tender chorle makſt waſt in niggarding: &lt;span class="break"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;   Pitty the world,or elſe this glutton be, &lt;span class="break"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;   To eate the worlds due,by the graue and thee.&lt;span class="break"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 17: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;A copy-and-pastable version of Shakespeare’s first sonnet (&lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cf." target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;cf.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt; &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-sonnet_1" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;12&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;By copying and pasting the text from the &lt;a href="https://www.learnenough.com/command-line-tutorial#fig-copy_paste_sonnet_1" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;HTML version&lt;/a&gt; of &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-copy_paste_sonnet_1" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;17&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, use &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; to make a file called &lt;code&gt;sonnet_1_complete.txt&lt;/code&gt; containing the full (original) text of Shakespeare’s first sonnet.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: You may recall getting stuck when &lt;code&gt;echo&lt;/code&gt; was followed by an unmatched double quote (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-our_first_command" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1.2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-getting_out_of_trouble" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), as in &lt;code&gt;echo "&lt;/code&gt;, but in fact this construction allows you to print out a multi-line block of text.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Just remember to put a closing quote at the end, and then redirect to a file with the appropriate name.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Check that the contents are correct using &lt;code&gt;cat&lt;/code&gt; (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-cat" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;14&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;). &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-copy-paste-to-file"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Type the sequence of commands needed to create an empty file called &lt;code&gt;foo&lt;/code&gt;, rename it to &lt;code&gt;bar&lt;/code&gt;, and copy it to &lt;code&gt;baz&lt;/code&gt;. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-create-rename-copy"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;What is the command to list only the files starting with the letter “b”?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: Use a wildcard. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-list-wildcard"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Remove both &lt;code&gt;bar&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;baz&lt;/code&gt; using a &lt;em&gt;single&lt;/em&gt; call to &lt;code&gt;rm&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: If those are the only two files in the current directory that start with the letter “b”, you can use the wildcard pattern from the previous exercise. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-rm-wildcard"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="sec-inspecting_files" data-tralics-id="cid3" class="section" data-number="3"&gt;&lt;h2&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-inspecting_files" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;3 &lt;/span&gt;Inspecting files&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Having seen how to create and manipulate files, now it’s time to learn how to examine their contents.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This is especially important for files too long to fit on a single screen.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In particular, we saw starting in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-redirecting_and_appending" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2.1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; how to use the &lt;code&gt;cat&lt;/code&gt; command to dump the file contents to the screen, but this doesn’t work very well for longer files.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-downloading_a_file" data-tralics-id="uid110" class="subsection" data-number="3.1"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-downloading_a_file" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;3.1 &lt;/span&gt;Downloading a file&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;To give us a place to start, rather than creating a long file by hand (which is cumbersome) we’ll download a file from the Internet using the powerful &lt;code&gt;curl&lt;/code&gt; utility (sometimes written as “cURL”), which allows us to interact with a URL&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-17" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-17"&gt;17&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; at the command line.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Although it’s not part of the core Unix command set, the &lt;code&gt;curl&lt;/code&gt; command is widely available on Unix systems.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To make sure it’s available on your system, we can use the &lt;code&gt;which&lt;/code&gt; command, which looks to see if the given program is available at the command line.&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-18" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-18"&gt;18&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The way to use it is to type &lt;code&gt;which&lt;/code&gt; followed by the name of the program—in this case, &lt;code&gt;curl&lt;/code&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; which curl&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;/usr/bin/curl&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;I’ve shown the output on my system (&lt;code&gt;/usr/bin/curl&lt;/code&gt;, usually read as “user bin curl”), but the result on your system may differ.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In particular, if the result is just a blank line, you will have to install &lt;code&gt;curl&lt;/code&gt;, which you can do by Googling for “install curl” followed by the name of your operating system.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Once &lt;code&gt;curl&lt;/code&gt; is installed, we can download a file called &lt;code&gt;sonnets.txt&lt;/code&gt; containing a large corpus of text using the command in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-curl" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;10&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-19" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-19"&gt;19&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-curl" data-tralics-id="uid114" data-number="10"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 10:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Using &lt;code&gt;curl&lt;/code&gt; to download a longer file.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; curl -OL cdn.learnenough.com/sonnets.txt&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls -rtl&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;Be sure to copy the command exactly; in particular, note that the option &lt;code&gt;-OL&lt;/code&gt; contains a capital letter “O” (&lt;code&gt;O&lt;/code&gt;) and not a zero (&lt;code&gt;0&lt;/code&gt;).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (Figuring out what these options do is left as an exercise (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-exercises_inspecting" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3.5.1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Also, on some systems (for mysterious reasons) you might have to run the command twice to get it to work; by inspecting the results of &lt;code&gt;ls -rtl&lt;/code&gt;, you should be able to tell if the initial call to &lt;code&gt;curl&lt;/code&gt; created the file &lt;code&gt;sonnets.txt&lt;/code&gt; as expected.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (If you do have to repeat the &lt;code&gt;curl&lt;/code&gt; command, you could press up arrow twice to retrieve it, but see &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-repeating_commands" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;9&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; for alternatives.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The result of running &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-curl" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;10&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; is &lt;code&gt;sonnets.txt&lt;/code&gt;, a file containing all 154 of Shakespeare’s sonnets.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This file contains 2620 lines, far too many to fit on one screen.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Learning how to inspect its contents is the goal of the rest of this section.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (Among other things, we’ll learn how to determine that it has 2620 lines without counting them all by hand.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="aside" id="aside-repeating_commands" data-tralics-id="uid115" data-number="9"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Box 9.&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Repeating previous commands&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Repeating previous commands is a frequent task when using the command line.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; So far in this tutorial, we’ve used the up-arrow key to retrieve (and possibly edit) previous commands, but this isn’t the only possibility.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; An even quicker way to find and immediately run a previous command involves using the exclamation point &lt;code class="tt"&gt;!&lt;/code&gt;, which in the context of software development is usually pronounced “bang”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To run the previous command exactly as written, we can use “bang bang”:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ echo "foo"&#x000A; foo&#x000A; $ !!&#x000A; echo "foo"&#x000A; foo&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;A closely related usage is “bang” followed by some number of characters, which runs the last command that started with those characters.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For example, to run the last &lt;code class="tt"&gt;curl&lt;/code&gt; command, we could type this:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ !curl&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;This would save us the trouble of typing out the options, the URL, etc.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Depending on our history of commands, the even terser &lt;code class="tt"&gt;!cu&lt;/code&gt; or &lt;code class="tt"&gt;!c&lt;/code&gt; would work as well.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This technique is especially useful when the desired command last happened many commands ago, which can make hitting up arrow cumbersome.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;A second and incredibly powerful technique is &lt;code class="tt"&gt;⌃R&lt;/code&gt;, which lets you search interactively through your previous commands, and then optionally edit the result before executing.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For example, we could try this to bring up the last &lt;code class="tt"&gt;curl&lt;/code&gt; command:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ &amp;lt;⌃R&amp;gt;&#x000A; (reverse-i-search)`&#x0027;: curl&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;On most systems, hitting return would then put the last &lt;code class="tt"&gt;curl&lt;/code&gt; command after our prompt and allow us to edit it (if desired) before hitting return to execute it.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; When your workflow happens to involve repeatedly running a variety of similar commands, sometimes it can seem like “all commands start with &lt;code class="tt"&gt;⌃R&lt;/code&gt;.”&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_downloading" data-tralics-id="uid116" class="subsubsection" data-number="3.1.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_downloading" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Use the command &lt;code&gt;curl -I https://www.learnenough.com/&lt;/code&gt; to fetch the &lt;em&gt;HTTP header&lt;/em&gt; for the Learn Enough website.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; What is the &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_HTTP_status_codes" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;HTTP status code&lt;/a&gt; for the address?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; How does this differ from the status code for &lt;code class="tt"&gt;learnenough.com&lt;/code&gt; (without the &lt;code&gt;https://&lt;/code&gt;)? &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-curl-i"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Using &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt;, confirm that &lt;code&gt;sonnets.txt&lt;/code&gt; exists on your system.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; How big is it in bytes?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: Recall from &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-listing" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2.2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; that the “long form” of &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; displays a byte count. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-ls-long-form"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;The byte count in the previous exercise is high enough that it’s more naturally thought of in &lt;em&gt;kilobytes&lt;/em&gt; (often treated as 1000 bytes, but actually equal to &lt;span class="inline_math"&gt;\( 2^{10} = 1024 \)&lt;/span&gt; bytes).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; By adding &lt;code&gt;-h&lt;/code&gt; (“human-readable”) option to &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt;, list the long form of the sonnets file with a human-readable byte count. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-ls-human"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Suppose you wanted to list the files and directories using &lt;strong&gt;h&lt;/strong&gt;uman-readable byte counts, &lt;strong&gt;a&lt;/strong&gt;ll, by &lt;strong&gt;r&lt;/strong&gt;everse &lt;strong&gt;t&lt;/strong&gt;ime-sorted &lt;strong&gt;l&lt;/strong&gt;ong-form.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; What command would you use?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Why might this command be the personal favorite of the author of this tutorial?&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-20" class="footnote intersentence"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-20"&gt;20&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-ls-hartl"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-making_heads_and_tails" data-tralics-id="uid122" class="subsection" data-number="3.2"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-making_heads_and_tails" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;3.2 &lt;/span&gt;Making heads and tails of it&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Two complementary commands for inspecting files are &lt;code&gt;head&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;tail&lt;/code&gt;, which respectively allow us to view the beginning (head) and end (tail) of the file.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The &lt;code&gt;head&lt;/code&gt; command shows the first 10 lines of the file (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-head" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;11&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-head" data-tralics-id="uid123" data-number="11"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 11:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Looking at the head of the sample text file.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="hll"&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; head sonnets.txt&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Shake-speare&#x0027;s Sonnets&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;I&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;From fairest creatures we desire increase,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;That thereby beauty&#x0027;s Rose might never die,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;But as the riper should by time decease,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;His tender heir might bear his memory:&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;But thou contracted to thine own bright eyes,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Feed&#x0027;st thy light&#x0027;s flame with self-substantial fuel&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;Similarly, &lt;code&gt;tail&lt;/code&gt; shows the last 10 lines of the file (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-tail" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;12&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-tail" data-tralics-id="uid124" data-number="12"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 12:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Looking at the tail of the sample text file.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="hll"&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; tail sonnets.txt&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="go"&gt;The fairest votary took up that fire&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Which many legions of true hearts had warm&#x0027;d;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;And so the general of hot desire&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Was, sleeping, by a virgin hand disarm&#x0027;d.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;This brand she quenched in a cool well by,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Which from Love&#x0027;s fire took heat perpetual,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Growing a bath and healthful remedy,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;For men diseas&#x0027;d; but I, my mistress&#x0027; thrall,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt; Came there for cure and this by that I prove,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt; Love&#x0027;s fire heats water, water cools not love.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;These two commands are useful when (as is often the case) you know for sure you only need to inspect the beginning or end of a file.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-wordcount_and_pipes" data-tralics-id="uid125" class="subsubsection" data-number="3.2.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-wordcount_and_pipes" class="heading"&gt;Wordcount and pipes&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;By the way, I didn’t recall offhand how many lines &lt;code&gt;head&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;tail&lt;/code&gt; show by default.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Since there are only 10 lines in the output, I could have counted them by hand, but in fact I was able to figure it out using the &lt;code&gt;wc&lt;/code&gt; command (short for “wordcount”; recall &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-y_u_no" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;16&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The most common use of &lt;code&gt;wc&lt;/code&gt; is on full files.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For example, we can run &lt;code&gt;sonnets.txt&lt;/code&gt; through &lt;code&gt;wc&lt;/code&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; wc sonnets.txt&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;  2620  17670  95635 sonnets.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Here the three numbers indicate how many lines, words, and bytes there are in the file, so there are 2620 lines (thereby fulfilling the promise made at the end of &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-downloading_a_file" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3.1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), 17670 words, and 95635 bytes.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;You are now in a position to be able to guess one method for determining how many lines are in &lt;code&gt;head sonnets.txt&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In particular, we can combine &lt;code&gt;head&lt;/code&gt; with the redirect operator (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-redirecting_and_appending" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2.1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) to make a file with the relevant contents, and then run &lt;code&gt;wc&lt;/code&gt; on it, as shown in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-head_redirected" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;13&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-head_redirected" data-tralics-id="uid126" data-number="13"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 13:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Redirecting &lt;code&gt;head&lt;/code&gt; and running &lt;code&gt;wc&lt;/code&gt; on the result.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; head sonnets.txt &amp;gt; sonnets_head.txt&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; wc sonnets_head.txt&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;   10   46   294 sonnets_head.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;We see from &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-head_redirected" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;13&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; that there are 10 lines in &lt;code&gt;head wc&lt;/code&gt; (along with 46 words and 294 bytes).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The same method, of course, would work for &lt;code&gt;tail&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;On the other hand, you might get the feeling that it’s a little unclean to make an intermediate file just to run &lt;code&gt;wc&lt;/code&gt; on it, and indeed there’s a way to avoid it using a technique called &lt;em&gt;pipes&lt;/em&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-head_pipe" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;14&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; shows how to do it.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-head_pipe" data-tralics-id="uid127" data-number="14"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 14:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Piping the result of &lt;code&gt;head&lt;/code&gt; through &lt;code&gt;wc&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; head sonnets.txt &lt;span class="p"&gt;|&lt;/span&gt; wc&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;   10   46   294&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;The command in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-head_pipe" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;14&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; runs &lt;code&gt;head sonnets.txt&lt;/code&gt; and then &lt;em&gt;pipes&lt;/em&gt; the result through &lt;code&gt;wc&lt;/code&gt; using the pipe symbol &lt;code&gt;|&lt;/code&gt; (Shift-backslash on most QWERTY keyboards).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The reason this works is that the &lt;code&gt;wc&lt;/code&gt; command, in addition to taking a filename as an argument, can (like many Unix programs) take input from “standard in” (compare to “standard out” mentioned in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-our_first_command" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1.2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), which in this case is the output of &lt;code&gt;head sonnets.txt&lt;/code&gt; shown in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-head" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;11&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The &lt;code&gt;wc&lt;/code&gt; program takes this input and counts it the same way it counts a file, yielding the same line, word, and byte counts as &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-head_redirected" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;13&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div
