id="sec-exercises_head_tails" data-tralics-id="uid128" class="subsubsection" data-number="3.2.2"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_head_tails" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;By piping the results of &lt;code&gt;tail sonnets.txt&lt;/code&gt; through &lt;code&gt;wc&lt;/code&gt;, confirm that (like &lt;code&gt;head&lt;/code&gt;) the &lt;code&gt;tail&lt;/code&gt; command outputs 10 lines by default. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-tail-wc"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;By running &lt;code&gt;man head&lt;/code&gt;, learn how to look at the first &lt;code&gt;n&lt;/code&gt; lines of the file.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; By experimenting with different values of &lt;code&gt;n&lt;/code&gt;, find a &lt;code&gt;head&lt;/code&gt; command to print out just enough lines to display the first sonnet in its entirety (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-sonnet_1" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;12&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;). &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-head-n"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Pipe the results of the previous exercise through &lt;code&gt;tail&lt;/code&gt; (with the appropriate options) to print out &lt;em&gt;only&lt;/em&gt; the 14 lines composing Sonnet 1.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: The command will look something like &lt;code&gt;head -n &amp;lt;i&amp;gt; sonnets.txt | tail -n &amp;lt;j&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;, where &lt;code&gt;&amp;lt;i&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;&amp;lt;j&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt; represent the numerical arguments to the &lt;code&gt;-n&lt;/code&gt; option. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-pipe-tail"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;One of the most useful applications of &lt;code&gt;tail&lt;/code&gt; is running &lt;code&gt;tail -f&lt;/code&gt; to view a file that’s actively changing.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This is especially common when monitoring files used to log the activity of, e.g., web servers, a practice known as “&lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tail_(Unix)#File_monitoring" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;tailing the log file&lt;/a&gt;”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To simulate the creation of a log file, run &lt;code&gt;ping learnenough.com &amp;gt; learnenough.log&lt;/code&gt; in one terminal tab.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (The &lt;code&gt;ping&lt;/code&gt; command “pings” a server to see if it’s working.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In a second tab, type the command to tail the log file.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (At this point, both tabs will be stuck, so once you’ve gotten the gist of &lt;code&gt;tail -f&lt;/code&gt; you should use the technique from &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-getting_out_of_trouble" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to get out of trouble.) &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-tail-f"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-less_is_more" data-tralics-id="uid133" class="subsection" data-number="3.3"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-less_is_more" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;3.3 &lt;/span&gt;Less is more&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Unix provides two utilities for the common task of wanting to look at more than just the head or tail of a file.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The older of these programs is called &lt;code&gt;more&lt;/code&gt;, but (I’d guess initially as a tongue-in-cheek joke) there’s a more powerful variant called &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-21" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-21"&gt;21&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt; program is interactive, so it’s hard to capture in print, but here’s roughly what it looks like:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; less sonnets.txt&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Shake-speare&#x0027;s Sonnets&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;I&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;From fairest creatures we desire increase,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;That thereby beauty&#x0027;s Rose might never die,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;But as the riper should by time decease,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;His tender heir might bear his memory:&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;But thou contracted to thine own bright eyes,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Feed&#x0027;st thy light&#x0027;s flame with self-substantial fuel,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Making a famine where abundance lies,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Thy self thy foe, to thy sweet self too cruel:&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Thou that art now the world&#x0027;s fresh ornament,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;And only herald to the gaudy spring,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Within thine own bud buriest thy content,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;And tender churl mak&#x0027;st waste in niggarding:&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt; Pity the world, or else this glutton be,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt; To eat the world&#x0027;s due, by the grave and thee.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;II&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;When forty winters shall besiege thy brow,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;And dig deep trenches in thy beauty&#x0027;s field,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="hll"&gt;&lt;span class="go"&gt;sonnets.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The point of &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt; is that it lets you navigate through the file in several useful ways, such as moving one line up or down with the arrow keys, pressing space bar to move a page down, pressing &lt;code&gt;⌃F&lt;/code&gt; to move forward a page (i.e., the same as spacebar) or &lt;code&gt;⌃B&lt;/code&gt; to move back a page.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To quit &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt;, type &lt;code&gt;q&lt;/code&gt; (for “quit”).&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-tudor_rose" data-tralics-id="uid135" data-number="18"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/tudor_rose.png" alt="images/figures/tudor_rose"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 18: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;A &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tudor_rose" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;famous rose&lt;/a&gt; from the time of Shakespeare.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Perhaps the most powerful aspect of &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt; is the forward slash key &lt;code&gt;/&lt;/code&gt;, which lets you search through the file from beginning to end.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For example, suppose we wanted to search through &lt;code&gt;sonnets.txt&lt;/code&gt; for “rose” (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-tudor_rose" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;18&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;),&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-22" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-22"&gt;22&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt; one of the most frequently used images used in the &lt;em&gt;Sonnets&lt;/em&gt;.&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-23" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-23"&gt;23&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The way to do this in &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt; is to type &lt;code&gt;/rose&lt;/code&gt; (read “slash rose”), as shown in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-rose_search" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;15&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-rose_search" data-tralics-id="uid138" data-number="15"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 15:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Searching for the string “rose” using &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Shake-speare&#x0027;s Sonnets&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;I&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;From fairest creatures we desire increase,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;That thereby beauty&#x0027;s Rose might never die,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;But as the riper should by time decease,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;His tender heir might bear his memory:&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;But thou contracted to thine own bright eyes,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Feed&#x0027;st thy light&#x0027;s flame with self-substantial fuel,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Making a famine where abundance lies,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Thy self thy foe, to thy sweet self too cruel:&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Thou that art now the world&#x0027;s fresh ornament,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;And only herald to the gaudy spring,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Within thine own bud buriest thy content,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;And tender churl mak&#x0027;st waste in niggarding:&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt; Pity the world, or else this glutton be,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt; To eat the world&#x0027;s due, by the grave and thee.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;II&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;When forty winters shall besiege thy brow,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;And dig deep trenches in thy beauty&#x0027;s field,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="hll"&gt;&lt;span class="go"&gt;/rose&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;The result of pressing return after typing &lt;code&gt;/rose&lt;/code&gt; in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-rose_search" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;15&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; is to highlight the first occurrence of “rose” in the file.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; You can then press &lt;code&gt;n&lt;/code&gt; to navigate to the next match, or &lt;code&gt;N&lt;/code&gt; to navigate to the previous match.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The last two essential &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt; less commands are &lt;code&gt;G&lt;/code&gt; to move to the end of the file and &lt;code&gt;1G&lt;/code&gt; (that’s &lt;code&gt;1&lt;/code&gt; followed by &lt;code&gt;G&lt;/code&gt;) to move back to the beginning.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#table-less_commands" class="hyperref"&gt;Table &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; summarizes what are in my view the most important key combinations (i.e., the ones I think you need to be &lt;em&gt;dangerous&lt;/em&gt;), but if you’re curious you can find a longer list of commands at the &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Less_(Unix)" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Wikipedia page on &lt;code class="tt"&gt;less&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;I encourage you to get in the habit of using &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt; as your go-to utility for looking at the contents of a file.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The skills you develop have other applications as well; for example, the man pages (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-man_pages" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1.3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) use the same interface as &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt;, so by learning about &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt; you’ll get better at navigating the man pages as well.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="table-less_commands" data-tralics-id="uid139" data-number="4" class="table"&gt;&lt;table class="tabular"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr class="bottom_border"&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Command&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Description&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Example&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;up &amp;amp; down arrow keys&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Move up or down one line&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;spacebar&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Move forward one page&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;⌃F&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Move forward one page&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;⌃B&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Move back one page&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;G&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Move to end of file&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;1G&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Move to beginning of file&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;/&amp;lt;string&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Search file for string&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;/rose&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;n&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Move to next search result&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;N&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Move to previous search result&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;q&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Quit &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Table 4: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;The most important &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt; commands.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_summary_less" data-tralics-id="uid140" class="subsubsection" data-number="3.3.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_summary_less" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Run &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt; on &lt;code&gt;sonnets.txt&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Go down three pages and then back up three pages.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Go to the end of the file, then to the beginning, then quit. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-less-pages"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Search for the string “All” (case-sensitive).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Go forward a few occurrences, then back a few occurrences.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Then go to the beginning of the file and count the occurrences by searching forward until you hit the end.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Compare your count to the result of running &lt;code&gt;grep All sonnets.txt | wc&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (We’ll learn about &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-grepping" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3.4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.) &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-less-grep"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Using &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;/&lt;/code&gt; (“slash”), find the sonnet that begins with the line “Let me not”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Are there any other occurrences of this string in the &lt;em&gt;Sonnets&lt;/em&gt;?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: Press &lt;code&gt;n&lt;/code&gt; to find the next occurrence (if any).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Extra credit&lt;/em&gt;: &lt;a href="https://youtu.be/bt7OynPUIY8" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Listen to the sonnet&lt;/a&gt; in both modern and &lt;a href="http://originalpronunciation.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;original pronunciation&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Which version’s rhyme scheme is better? &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-less-slash"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Because &lt;code&gt;man&lt;/code&gt; uses &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt;, we are now in a position to search man pages interactively.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; By searching for the string “sort” in the man page for &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt;, discover the option to sort files by size.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; What is the command to display the long form of files sorted so the largest files appear at the bottom?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: Use &lt;code&gt;ls -rtl&lt;/code&gt; as a model. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-man-slash"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-grepping" data-tralics-id="uid145" class="subsection" data-number="3.4"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-grepping" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;3.4 &lt;/span&gt;Grepping&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;One of the most powerful tools for inspecting file contents is &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt;, which probably stands for something, but it’s not important what.&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-24" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-24"&gt;24&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Indeed, &lt;em&gt;grep&lt;/em&gt; is frequently used as a verb, as in “You should totally grep that file.”&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The most common use of &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; is just to search for a substring in a file.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For example, we saw in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-less_is_more" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3.3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; how to use &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt; to search for the string “rose” in Shakespeare’s sonnets.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Using &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt;, we can find the references directly, as shown in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-grep_rose" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;16&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-grep_rose" data-tralics-id="uid147" data-number="16"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 16:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Finding the occurrences of “rose” in Shakespeare’s sonnets.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; grep rose sonnets.txt&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;The rose looks fair, but fairer we it deem&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;As the perfumed tincture of the roses.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Die to themselves. Sweet roses do not so;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Roses of shadow, since his rose is true?&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Which, like a canker in the fragrant rose,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;Nor praise the deep vermilion in the rose;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;The roses fearfully on thorns did stand,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt; Save thou, my rose, in it thou art my all.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;I have seen roses damask&#x0027;d, red and white,&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;But no such roses see I in her cheeks;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;With the command in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-grep_rose" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;16&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, it appears that we are in a position to count the number of lines containing references to the word “rose” by piping to &lt;code&gt;wc&lt;/code&gt; (as in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-less_is_more" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3.3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), as shown in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-grep_rose_wc" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;17&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-grep_rose_wc" data-tralics-id="uid148" data-number="17"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 17:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Piping the results of &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; to &lt;code&gt;wc&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; grep rose sonnets.txt &lt;span class="p"&gt;|&lt;/span&gt; wc&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;   10   82   419&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-grep_rose_wc" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;17&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; tells us that 10 lines contain “rose” (or “roses”, since “rose” is a substring of “roses”).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; But you may recall from &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-sonnet_1" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;12&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; that Shakespeare’s first sonnet contains “Rose” with a &lt;em&gt;capital&lt;/em&gt; “R”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Referring to &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-grep_rose" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;16&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, we see that this line has in fact been missed.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This is because &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; is case-sensitive by default, and “rose” doesn’t match “Rose”.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;As you might suspect, &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; has an option to perform case-insensitive matching as well.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; One way to figure it out is to search through the &lt;code&gt;man&lt;/code&gt; page for &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ul&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Type &lt;code&gt;man grep&lt;/code&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Type &lt;code&gt;/case&lt;/code&gt; and then return&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Read off the result (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-man_grep" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;19&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;)&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;(As noted briefly in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-man_pages" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1.3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, the man pages use the same interface as the &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt; command we met in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-less_is_more" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3.3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, so we can search through them using &lt;code&gt;/&lt;/code&gt;.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-man_grep" data-tralics-id="uid152" data-number="19"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/man_grep.png" alt="images/figures/man_grep"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 19: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;The result of searching &lt;code&gt;man grep&lt;/code&gt; for “case”.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Applying the result of the above procedure yields &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-grep_i_wc" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;18&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Comparing the results of &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-grep_i_wc" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;18&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; with &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-grep_rose_wc" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;17&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, we see that we now have 12 matching lines instead of only 10, so there must be a total of &lt;span class="inline_math"&gt;\( 12-10=2 \)&lt;/span&gt; lines containing “Rose” (but not “rose”) in the &lt;em&gt;Sonnets&lt;/em&gt;.&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-25" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-25"&gt;25&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-grep_i_wc" data-tralics-id="uid154" data-number="18"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 18:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Doing a case-insensitive grep.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; grep -i rose sonnets.txt &lt;span class="p"&gt;|&lt;/span&gt; wc&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;   12   96   508&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;The &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; utility is insanely powerful, especially when combined with so-called &lt;em&gt;regular expressions&lt;/em&gt;, but learning &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;grep -i&lt;/code&gt; are &lt;em&gt;almost&lt;/em&gt; enough to be dangerous (including the important application of &lt;em&gt;grepping processes&lt;/em&gt; (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-ps_aux" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;10&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;)).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; We’ll see the third and final &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; variant needed to be dangerous in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-directories" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="aside" id="aside-ps_aux" data-tralics-id="uid155" data-number="10"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Box 10.&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Grepping processes&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;One of the many uses of &lt;code class="tt"&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; is filtering the Unix &lt;em&gt;process list&lt;/em&gt; for running programs that match a particular string.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (On Unix-like systems such as Linux and macOS, user and system tasks each take place within a well-defined container called a &lt;em&gt;process&lt;/em&gt;.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This is especially useful when there’s a rogue process on your system that needs to be killed.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (A good way to find such processes is by running the &lt;code class="tt"&gt;top&lt;/code&gt; command, which shows the processes consuming the most resources.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;For example, at one point in the &lt;a href="http://railstutorial.org/book" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Ruby on Rails Tutorial&lt;/em&gt; book&lt;/a&gt;, it’s important to eliminate a program called &lt;code class="tt"&gt;spring&lt;/code&gt; from the process list.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To do this, first the processes need to be found, and the way to see all the processes on your system is to use the &lt;code class="tt"&gt;ps&lt;/code&gt; command with the &lt;code class="tt"&gt;aux&lt;/code&gt; options:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ ps aux&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Per &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-y_u_no" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;16&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;code class="tt"&gt;ps&lt;/code&gt; is short for “process status”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; And for &lt;a href="http://www.freebsd.org/cgi/man.cgi?query=ps&amp;amp;manpath=SuSE+Linux/i386+11.3" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;confusing and obscure reasons&lt;/a&gt;, options to &lt;code class="tt"&gt;ps&lt;/code&gt; aren’t written with a dash (so it’s &lt;code class="tt"&gt;ps aux&lt;/code&gt; instead of &lt;code class="tt"&gt;ps -aux&lt;/code&gt;).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (How on earth are you supposed to know this?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; That’s what this tutorial is for.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;To filter the processes by program name, you pipe the results of &lt;code class="tt"&gt;ps&lt;/code&gt; through the &lt;code class="tt"&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ ps aux | grep spring&#x000A; ubuntu 12241 0.3 0.5 589960 178416 ? Ssl Sep20 1:46&#x000A; spring app | sample_app | started 7 hours ago&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The result shown gives some details about the process, but the most important thing is the first number, which is the &lt;em&gt;process id&lt;/em&gt;, or pid (often pronounced to rhyme with “kid”).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To eliminate an unwanted process, we use the &lt;code class="tt"&gt;kill&lt;/code&gt; command to issue the Unix terminate code (which &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unix_signal#List_of_signals" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;happens to be 15&lt;/a&gt;) to the pid:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ kill -15 12241&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;This is the technique I recommend for killing individual processes, such as a rogue web server (with the pid found via &lt;code class="tt"&gt;ps aux | grep server&lt;/code&gt;), but sometimes it’s convenient to kill all the processes matching a particular process name, such as when you want to kill all the &lt;code class="tt"&gt;spring&lt;/code&gt; processes gunking up your system.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In this case, you can kill all the processes with name &lt;code class="tt"&gt;spring&lt;/code&gt; using the &lt;code class="tt"&gt;pkill&lt;/code&gt; command as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ pkill -15 -f spring&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Any time something isn’t behaving as expected, or a process appears to be frozen, it’s a good idea to run &lt;code class="tt"&gt;top&lt;/code&gt; or &lt;code class="tt"&gt;ps aux&lt;/code&gt; to see what’s going on, pipe &lt;code class="tt"&gt;ps aux&lt;/code&gt; through &lt;code class="tt"&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; to select the suspected processes, and then run &lt;code class="tt"&gt;kill -15 &amp;lt;pid&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt; or &lt;code class="tt"&gt;pkill -15 -f &amp;lt;name&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt; to clear things up.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_grep" data-tralics-id="uid156" class="subsubsection" data-number="3.4.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_grep" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;By searching &lt;code&gt;man grep&lt;/code&gt; for “line number”, construct a command to find the line numbers in &lt;code&gt;sonnets.txt&lt;/code&gt; where the string “rose” appears. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-grep-command"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;You should find that the last occurrences of “rose” is (via “roses”) on line 2203.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Figure out how to go directly to this line when running &lt;code&gt;less sonnets.txt&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: Recall from &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#table-less_commands" class="hyperref"&gt;Table &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; that &lt;code&gt;1G&lt;/code&gt; goes to the top of the file, i.e., line 1.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Similarly, &lt;code&gt;17G&lt;/code&gt; goes to line 17.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Etc. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-less-command-jump"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;By piping the output of &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; to &lt;code&gt;head&lt;/code&gt;, print out the first (and &lt;em&gt;only&lt;/em&gt; the first) line in &lt;code&gt;sonnets.txt&lt;/code&gt; containing “rose”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: Use the result of the second exercise in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-exercises_head_tails" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3.2.2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-grep-head"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;In &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-grep_i_wc" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;18&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, we saw two additional lines that case-insensitively matched “rose”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Execute a command confirming that both of the lines contain the string “Rose” (and not, e.g., “rOSe”).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: Use a case-sensitive &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; for “Rose”. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-grep-case"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;You should find in the previous exercise that there are &lt;em&gt;three&lt;/em&gt; lines matching “Rose” instead of the two you might have expected from &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-grep_i_wc" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;18&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This is because there is one line that contains both “Rose” &lt;em&gt;and&lt;/em&gt; “rose”, and thus shows up in both &lt;code&gt;grep rose&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;grep -i rose&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Write a command confirming that the number of lines matching “Rose” but &lt;em&gt;not&lt;/em&gt; matching “rose” is equal to the expected 2.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: Pipe the result of &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; to &lt;code&gt;grep -v&lt;/code&gt;, and then pipe that result to &lt;code&gt;wc&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (What does &lt;code&gt;-v&lt;/code&gt; do?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Read the man page for &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-technical_sophistication" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).) &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-grep-pipe-wc"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-summary_inspecting" data-tralics-id="uid162" class="subsection" data-number="3.5"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-summary_inspecting" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;3.5 &lt;/span&gt;Summary&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Important commands from this section are summarized in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#table-inspecting_files" class="hyperref"&gt;Table &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="table-inspecting_files" data-tralics-id="uid163" data-number="5" class="table"&gt;&lt;table class="tabular"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr class="bottom_border"&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Command&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Description&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Example&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;curl&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Interact with URLs&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ curl -O example.com&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;which&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Locate a program on the path&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ which curl&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;head &amp;lt;file&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Display first part of file&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ head
