class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;wc &amp;lt;file&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Count lines, words, bytes&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ wc foo&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;cmd1 | cmd2&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Pipe &lt;code class="tt"&gt;cmd1&lt;/code&gt; to &lt;code class="tt"&gt;cmd2&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ head foo | wc&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;ping &amp;lt;url&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Ping a server URL&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ ping google.com&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;less &amp;lt;file&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;View file contents interactively&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ less foo&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;grep &amp;lt;string&amp;gt; &amp;lt;file&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Find string in file&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ grep foo bar.txt&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;grep -i &amp;lt;string&amp;gt; &amp;lt;file&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Find case-insensitively&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ grep -i foo bar.txt&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;ps&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Show processes&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ ps aux&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;top&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Show processes (sorted)&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ top&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;kill -&amp;lt;level&amp;gt; &amp;lt;pid&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Kill a process&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ kill -15 24601&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;pkill -&amp;lt;level&amp;gt; -f &amp;lt;name&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Kill matching processes&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ pkill -15 -f spring&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Table 5: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Important commands from &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-inspecting_files" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_inspecting" data-tralics-id="uid164" class="subsubsection" data-number="3.5.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_inspecting" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;The &lt;code&gt;history&lt;/code&gt; command prints the history of commands in a particular terminal shell (subject to some limit, which is typically large).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Pipe &lt;code&gt;history&lt;/code&gt; to &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt; to examine your command history.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; What was your 17th command? &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-history-pipe-grep"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;By piping the output of &lt;code&gt;history&lt;/code&gt; to &lt;code&gt;wc&lt;/code&gt;, count how many commands you’ve executed so far. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-history-pipe-wc"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;One use of &lt;code&gt;history&lt;/code&gt; is to grep your commands to find useful ones you’ve used before, with each command preceded by the corresponding number in the command history.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; By piping the output of &lt;code&gt;history&lt;/code&gt; to &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt;, determine the number for the last occurrence of &lt;code&gt;curl&lt;/code&gt;. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-history-pipe-grep-curl"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;In &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-repeating_commands" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;9&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, we learned about &lt;code&gt;!!&lt;/code&gt; (“bang bang”) to execute the previous command.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Similarly, &lt;code&gt;!n&lt;/code&gt; executes command number &lt;code&gt;n&lt;/code&gt;, so that, e.g., &lt;code&gt;!17&lt;/code&gt; executes the 17th command in the command history.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Use the result from the previous exercise to re-run the last occurrence of &lt;code&gt;curl&lt;/code&gt;. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-bang-bang"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;What do the &lt;code&gt;O&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;L&lt;/code&gt; options in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-curl" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;10&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; mean?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: Pipe the output of &lt;code&gt;curl -h&lt;/code&gt; to &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt; and search first for the string &lt;code&gt;-O&lt;/code&gt; and then for the string &lt;code&gt;-L&lt;/code&gt;. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-curl-opts"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="sec-directories" data-tralics-id="cid4" class="section" data-number="4"&gt;&lt;h2&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-directories" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;4 &lt;/span&gt;Directories&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Having examined many of Unix utilities for dealing with files, the time has come to learn about &lt;em&gt;directories&lt;/em&gt;, sometimes known by the synonym &lt;em&gt;folders&lt;/em&gt; (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-directory_folder" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;20&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As we’ll see, many of the ideas developed in the context of files also apply to directories, but there are many differences as well.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-structure" data-tralics-id="uid170" class="subsection" data-number="4.1"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-structure" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;4.1 &lt;/span&gt;Directory structure&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The structure of Unix-style directories is typically indicated using a list of directory names separated by forward slashes, which we can combine with the &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; command (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-listing" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2.2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) like this:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls /Users/mhartl/ruby&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;or like this:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls /usr/local/bin&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;As seen in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-directory_folder" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;20&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, these representations correspond to directories in a hierarchical filesystem, with (say) &lt;code&gt;mhartl&lt;/code&gt; a subdirectory of &lt;code&gt;Users&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;ruby&lt;/code&gt; a subdirectory of &lt;code&gt;mhartl&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-directory_folder" data-tralics-id="uid171" data-number="20"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/directory_folder.png" alt="images/figures/directory_folder"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 20: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;The correspondence between folders &amp;amp; directories.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Conventions vary when speaking about directories: a &lt;em&gt;user directory&lt;/em&gt; like &lt;code&gt;/Users/mhartl&lt;/code&gt; would probably be read as “slash users slash mhartl” or “slash users mhartl”, whereas omitting the initial slash in spoken language is common for &lt;em&gt;system directories&lt;/em&gt; such as &lt;code&gt;/usr/local/bin&lt;/code&gt;, which would probably be pronounced “user local bin”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Because &lt;em&gt;all&lt;/em&gt; Unix directories are ultimately subdirectories of the &lt;em&gt;root directory&lt;/em&gt; &lt;code&gt;/&lt;/code&gt; (pronounced “slash”), the leading and separator slashes are implied.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Note&lt;/em&gt;: Referring to forward slashes incorrectly as “backslashes” is a &lt;a href="https://m.xkcd.com/727/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;cause of suffering&lt;/a&gt;, and should be strictly avoided.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The most important directory for a particular user is the &lt;em&gt;home directory&lt;/em&gt;, which on my macOS system is &lt;code&gt;/Users/mhartl&lt;/code&gt;, corresponding to my username (&lt;code&gt;mhartl&lt;/code&gt;).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The home directory can be specified as an &lt;em&gt;absolute path&lt;/em&gt;, as in &lt;code&gt;/Users/mhartl&lt;/code&gt;, or using the shorthand for the home directory is the tilde character &lt;code&gt;~&lt;/code&gt; (which is typed using Shift-backtick, located just to the left of the number 1 on most keyboards).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As a result, the two paths shown in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-directory_folder" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;20&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; are identical: &lt;code&gt;/Users/mhartl/ruby/projects&lt;/code&gt; is the same as &lt;code&gt;~/ruby/projects&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (Amusingly, the reason the tilde character is used for the home directory is simply because the “Home” key was the same as the key for producing “~” on &lt;a href="http://unix.stackexchange.com/questions/34196/why-was-chosen-to-represent-the-home-directory" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;some early keyboards&lt;/a&gt;.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;In addition to user directories, every Unix system has &lt;em&gt;system directories&lt;/em&gt; for the programs essential for the computer’s normal operation.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Modifying system files or directories requires special powers granted only to the &lt;em&gt;superuser&lt;/em&gt;, known as &lt;code&gt;root&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (This use of “root” is unrelated to the “root directory” mentioned above.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The superuser is so powerful that it’s considered bad form to log in as &lt;code&gt;root&lt;/code&gt;; instead, tasks executed as &lt;code&gt;root&lt;/code&gt; should typically use the &lt;code&gt;sudo&lt;/code&gt; command (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-sudo" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;11&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-26" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-26"&gt;26&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="aside" id="aside-sudo" data-tralics-id="uid173" data-number="11"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Box 11.&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;“&lt;code class="tt"&gt;sudo&lt;/code&gt; make me a sandwich.”&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;sudo&lt;/code&gt; gives ordinary users the power to execute commands as the superuser.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For example, let’s try &lt;code class="tt"&gt;touch&lt;/code&gt;ing a file in the system directory &lt;code class="tt"&gt;/opt&lt;/code&gt; as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ touch /opt/foo&#x000A; touch: /opt/foo: Permission denied&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Because normal users don’t have permission to modify &lt;code class="tt"&gt;/opt&lt;/code&gt;, the command fails, but it succeeds with &lt;code class="tt"&gt;sudo&lt;/code&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ sudo touch /opt/foo&#x000A; Password:&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;As shown, after entering &lt;code class="tt"&gt;sudo&lt;/code&gt; we are prompted to enter our user password; if entered correctly, and if the user has been configured to have &lt;code class="tt"&gt;sudo&lt;/code&gt; privileges (which is the default on most desktop Unix systems), then the command will succeed.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As shown in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-sandwich" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;21&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, this pattern of being denied at first, only to succeed using &lt;code class="tt"&gt;sudo&lt;/code&gt;, is a common theme in computing.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;To check that the file really was created, we can &lt;code class="tt"&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; it:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ ls -l /opt/foo&#x000A; -rw-r--r-- 1 root wheel 0 Jul 23 19:13 /opt/foo&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Note that (1) a normal user can &lt;code class="tt"&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; a file in a system directory (without &lt;code class="tt"&gt;sudo&lt;/code&gt;) and (2) the name &lt;code class="tt"&gt;root&lt;/code&gt; appears in the listing, indicating that the superuser owns the file.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (The meaning of the second term, &lt;code class="tt"&gt;wheel&lt;/code&gt;, is a little obscure, but you can learn about it on a site called, appropriately enough, &lt;a href="http://superuser.com/questions/191955/what-is-the-wheel-user-in-os-x" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;superuser&lt;/a&gt;.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;To remove the file we just created, we again need superuser status:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ rm -f /opt/foo&#x000A; rm: /opt/foo: Permission denied&#x000A; $ sudo !!&#x000A; $ !ls&#x000A; ls: /opt/foo: No such file or directory&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Here the first &lt;code class="tt"&gt;rm&lt;/code&gt; fails, so we’ve run &lt;code class="tt"&gt;sudo !!&lt;/code&gt;, which runs &lt;code class="tt"&gt;sudo&lt;/code&gt; and then the previous command , and we’ve followed that up with &lt;code class="tt"&gt;!ls&lt;/code&gt;, which runs the previous &lt;code class="tt"&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; command (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-repeating_commands" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;9&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;It’s also worth noting the English pronunciation of something like &lt;code class="tt"&gt;sudo !!&lt;/code&gt;, which is important when communicating via spoken language.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As noted in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-repeating_commands" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;9&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;code class="tt"&gt;!!&lt;/code&gt; is pronounced “bang bang”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;code class="tt"&gt;sudo&lt;/code&gt;, meanwhile, is pronounced either “SOO-doo” or “SOO-doh”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Both pronunciations are common, though I prefer the former because the &lt;code class="tt"&gt;do&lt;/code&gt; in &lt;code class="tt"&gt;sudo&lt;/code&gt; is in fact just the English word “do”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Thus, my preferred pronunciation for &lt;code class="tt"&gt;sudo !!&lt;/code&gt; is “SOO-doo bang bang”.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;By the way, the &lt;code class="tt"&gt;su&lt;/code&gt; in &lt;code class="tt"&gt;sudo&lt;/code&gt; &lt;a href="https://pthree.org/2009/12/31/the-meaning-of-su/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;originally stood&lt;/a&gt; for “super-user”, but over time its use expanded, and now is usually thought of as “substitute user”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;code class="tt"&gt;sudo&lt;/code&gt; is therefore a contraction of “substitute user do”, with the substitute user being the superuser by default.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Because the superuser can do anything, the command “sudo make me a sandwich” in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-sandwich" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;21&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; succeeds when a mere “make me a sandwich” does not.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-sandwich" data-tralics-id="uid174" data-number="21"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/sandwich.png" alt="images/figures/sandwich"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 21: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;“&lt;a href="https://m.xkcd.com/149/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Sandwich&lt;/a&gt;” (via &lt;a href="http://xkcd.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;xkcd&lt;/a&gt;) derives humor from the behavior of &lt;code&gt;sudo&lt;/code&gt;.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_structure" data-tralics-id="uid175" class="subsubsection" data-number="4.1.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_structure" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Write in words how you might speak the directory &lt;code&gt;~/foo/bar&lt;/code&gt;. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-speak-dir"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;In &lt;code&gt;/Users/bill/sonnets&lt;/code&gt;, what is the home directory?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; What is the username?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Which directory is deepest in the hierarchy? &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-dir-comp"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;For a user with username &lt;code&gt;bill&lt;/code&gt;, how do &lt;code&gt;/Users/bill/sonnets&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;~/sonnets&lt;/code&gt; differ (if at all)? &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-dir-username"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-making_directories" data-tralics-id="uid179" class="subsection" data-number="4.2"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-making_directories" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;4.2 &lt;/span&gt;Making directories&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;So far in this tutorial, we’ve created (and removed) a large number of text files.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The time has finally come to make a directory to contain them.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Although most modern operating systems include a graphical interface for this task, the Unix way to do it is with &lt;code&gt;mkdir&lt;/code&gt; (short for “make directory”, per &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-y_u_no" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;16&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;):&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; mkdir text_files&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Having made the directory, we can move the text files there using a wildcard:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; mv *.txt text_files/&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;We can confirm the move worked by listing the directory:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls text_files/&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;sonnet_1.txt     sonnet_1_reversed.txt sonnets.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;(Depending on how closely you’ve followed this tutorial, your results may vary.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;By default, running &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; on a directory shows its &lt;em&gt;contents&lt;/em&gt;, but we can show just the directory using the &lt;code&gt;-d&lt;/code&gt; option:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls -d text_files/&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;text_files/&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;This usage is especially common with the &lt;code&gt;-l&lt;/code&gt; option (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-listing" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2.2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;):&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls -ld text_files/&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;drwxr-xr-x 7 mhartl staff 238 Jul 24 18:07 text_files&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Finally, we can change directories using &lt;code&gt;cd&lt;/code&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt; text_files/&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Note that &lt;code&gt;cd&lt;/code&gt; typically supports tab completion, so (as described in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-tab_completion" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;8&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) we can actually type &lt;code&gt;cd tex⇥&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;After running &lt;code&gt;cd&lt;/code&gt;, we can confirm that we’re in the correct directory using the “print working directory” command, &lt;code&gt;pwd&lt;/code&gt;, together with another call to &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;pwd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;/Users/mhartl/text_files&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;sonnet_1.txt     sonnet_1_reversed.txt sonnets.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;These last steps of typing &lt;code&gt;pwd&lt;/code&gt; to double-check the directory, and especially running &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; to inspect the directory contents, are a matter of habit for many a grizzled command-line veteran.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (Your result for &lt;code&gt;pwd&lt;/code&gt; will, of course, be different, unless you happen to be using the username “mhartl” on macOS.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_making_dirctories" data-tralics-id="uid180" class="subsubsection" data-number="4.2.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_making_dirctories" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;What is the option for making intermediate directories as required, so that you can create, e.g., &lt;code&gt;~/foo&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;~/foo/bar&lt;/code&gt; with a single command?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: Refer to the man page for &lt;code&gt;mkdir&lt;/code&gt;. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-mkdir-p"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Use the option from the previous exercise to make the directory &lt;code&gt;foo&lt;/code&gt; and, within it, the directory &lt;code&gt;bar&lt;/code&gt; (i.e., &lt;code&gt;~/foo/bar&lt;/code&gt;) with a single command. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-mkdir-heirarchy"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;By piping the output of &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; to &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt;, list everything in the home directory that contains the letter “o”. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-ls-pipe-grep"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-navigating_directories" data-tralics-id="uid184" class="subsection" data-number="4.3"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-navigating_directories" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;4.3 &lt;/span&gt;Navigating directories&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;We saw in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-making_directories" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4.2&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; how to use &lt;code&gt;cd&lt;/code&gt; to change to a directory with a given name.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This is one of the most common ways of navigating, but there are a couple of special forms worth knowing.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The first is changing to the directory one level up in the hierarchy using &lt;code&gt;cd ..&lt;/code&gt; (read “see-dee dot-dot”):&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;pwd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;/Users/mhartl/text_files&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt; ..&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;pwd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;/Users/mhartl&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;In this case, because &lt;code&gt;/Users/mhartl&lt;/code&gt; is my &lt;em&gt;home directory&lt;/em&gt;, we could have accomplished the same thing using &lt;code&gt;cd&lt;/code&gt; by itself:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt; text_files/&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;pwd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;/Users/mhartl/text_files&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;pwd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;/Users/mhartl&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The reason this works is that &lt;code&gt;cd&lt;/code&gt; by itself changes to the user’s home directory, wherever that is.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This means that&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;and&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt; ~&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;are equivalent.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;When changing directories, it’s frequently useful to be able to specify the home directory somehow.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For example, suppose we make a second directory and cd into it:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;pwd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;/Users/mhartl&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; mkdir second_directory&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt; second_directory/&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Now if we want to change to the &lt;code&gt;text_files&lt;/code&gt; directory, we can &lt;code&gt;cd&lt;/code&gt; to &lt;code&gt;text_files&lt;/code&gt; via the home directory &lt;code&gt;~&lt;/code&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;pwd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;/Users/mhartl/second_directory&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt; ~/text_files&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;pwd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;/Users/mhartl/text_files&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Incidentally, we’re now in a position to understand the prompts shown in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-command_exercise" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;6&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;: I have my prompt configured to show the current directory, which might be something like &lt;code&gt;[~]&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;[ruby]&lt;/code&gt;, or &lt;code&gt;[projects]&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (We’ll discuss how to customize the prompt in &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/text-editor-tutorial" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Learn Enough Text Editor to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Especially eager (or impatient) readers can exercise their technical sophistication (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-technical_sophistication" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) by &lt;a href="http://lmgtfy.com/?q=bash+customize+prompt" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Googling for how to do it&lt;/a&gt;.)&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Closely related to &lt;code&gt;..&lt;/code&gt; for “one directory up” is &lt;code&gt;.&lt;/code&gt; (read “dot”) which means “the current directory”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The most common use of &lt;code&gt;.&lt;/code&gt; is when moving or copying files to the current directory:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;pwd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;/Users/mhartl/text_files&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt; ~/second_directory&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; cp ~/text_files/sonnets.txt .&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;sonnets.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Note in that the first call to &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; returns nothing, because &lt;code&gt;second_directory&lt;/code&gt; is initially empty.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Another common use of &lt;code&gt;.&lt;/code&gt; is in conjunction with the &lt;code&gt;find&lt;/code&gt; command, which like &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; is insanely powerful, but in my own use it looks like this 99% of the time:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; find . -name &lt;span class="s1"&gt;&#x0027;*.txt&#x0027;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;./text_files/sonnet_1.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;./text_files/sonnet_1_reversed.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;./text_files/sonnets.txt&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;In words, what this does is find files whose names match the pattern &lt;code&gt;*.txt&lt;/code&gt;, starting in the current directory &lt;code&gt;.&lt;/code&gt; and then in its subdirectories.&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-27" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-27"&gt;27&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The &lt;code&gt;find&lt;/code&gt; utility is incredibly useful for finding a misplaced file at the command line.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Perhaps my favorite use of &lt;code&gt;.&lt;/code&gt; is in “open dot”, which will work only on macOS:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt; ~/ruby/projects&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; open .&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The remarkable &lt;code&gt;open&lt;/code&gt; command opens its argument using whatever the default program is for the given file or directory.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (A similar command, &lt;code&gt;xdg-open&lt;/code&gt;, works on some Linux systems.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For example, &lt;code&gt;open foo.pdf&lt;/code&gt; would open the PDF file with the default viewer (which is Preview on most Macs).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In the case of a directory such as &lt;code&gt;.&lt;/code&gt;, that default program is the Finder, so &lt;code&gt;open .&lt;/code&gt; produces a result like that shown in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-directory_folder" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;20&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;A final navigational command, and one of my personal favorites, is &lt;code&gt;cd -&lt;/code&gt;, which cds to the &lt;em&gt;previous&lt;/em&gt; directory, wherever it was:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;pwd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;/Users/mhartl/second_directory&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt; ~/text_files&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;pwd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;/Users/mhartl/text_files&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt; -&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;/Users/mhartl/second_directory&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;I find that &lt;code&gt;cd -&lt;/code&gt; is especially useful when combining commands, as described in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-combining_commands" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;12&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="aside" id="aside-combining_commands" data-tralics-id="uid186" data-number="12"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Box 12.&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Combining commands&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;It’s often convenient to combine commands at the command line, such as when installing software using the Unix programs &lt;code class="tt"&gt;configure&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code class="tt"&gt;make&lt;/code&gt;, which often appear in the following sequence:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ ./configure ; make ; make install&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;This line runs the &lt;code class="tt"&gt;configure&lt;/code&gt; program from the current directory &lt;code class="tt"&gt;.&lt;/code&gt;, and then runs both &lt;code class="tt"&gt;make&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code class="tt"&gt;make install&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (You are not expected to understand what these programs do, and indeed they won’t work on your system unless you happen to be in the directory of a program designed to be installed this way.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Because they are separated by the semicolon character &lt;code class="tt"&gt;;&lt;/code&gt;, three commands are run in sequence.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;An even better way to combine commands is with the double-ampersand &lt;code class="tt"&gt;&amp;amp;&amp;amp;&lt;/code&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ ./configure &amp;amp;&amp;amp; make &amp;amp;&amp;amp; make install&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The difference is that commands separated by &lt;code class="tt"&gt;&amp;amp;&amp;amp;&lt;/code&gt; run only if the previous command &lt;em&gt;succeeded&lt;/em&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In contrast, with &lt;code class="tt"&gt;;&lt;/code&gt; all the commands will be run no matter what, which will cause an error in the likely case that subsequent commands depend on the results of the ones that precede them.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;I especially like to use &lt;code class="tt"&gt;&amp;amp;&amp;amp;&lt;/code&gt; in combination with &lt;code class="tt"&gt;cd -&lt;/code&gt;, which lets me do things like this:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;pre&gt; $ build_article &amp;amp;&amp;amp; cd ~/tau &amp;amp;&amp;amp; deploy &amp;amp;&amp;amp; cd -&lt;/pre&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Again, you are not expected to understand these commands, but the general idea is that we can (say) build an article in one directory, &lt;code class="tt"&gt;cd&lt;/code&gt; to a different directory, deploy (perhaps a &lt;a href="http://tauday.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;website&lt;/a&gt;) to production, and then &lt;code class="tt"&gt;cd&lt;/code&gt; back (&lt;code class="tt"&gt;cd -&lt;/code&gt;) to the original directory, where we can continue our work.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Then, if need be, we can just use up arrow (or one of the techniques from &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-repeating_commands" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;9&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) to retrieve the whole thing and do it all again.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_navigating_directories" data-tralics-id="uid187" class="subsubsection" data-number="4.3.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_navigating_directories" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;How do the effects of &lt;code&gt;cd&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;cd ~&lt;/code&gt; differ (or do they)? &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-cd-tilde"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Change to &lt;code&gt;text_files&lt;/code&gt;, then change to &lt;code&gt;second_directory&lt;/code&gt; using the “one directory up” double dot operator &lt;code&gt;..&lt;/code&gt;. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-cd-double-dot"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;From wherever you are, create an empty file called &lt;code&gt;nil&lt;/code&gt; in &lt;code&gt;text_files&lt;/code&gt; using whatever method you wish. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-create-empty-file"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Remove &lt;code&gt;nil&lt;/code&gt; from the previous exercise using a different path from the one you used before.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (In other words, if you used the path &lt;code&gt;~/text_files&lt;/code&gt; before, use something like &lt;code&gt;../text_files&lt;/code&gt; or &lt;code&gt;/Users/&amp;lt;username&amp;gt;/text_files&lt;/code&gt;.) &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-remove-empty-file"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-removing_directories" data-tralics-id="uid192" class="subsection" data-number="4.4"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-removing_directories" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;4.4 &lt;/span&gt;Renaming, copying, and deleting directories&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The commands for renaming, copying, and deleting directories are similar to those for files (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-renaming_copying_deleting" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;2.3&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), but there are some subtle differences worth noting.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The command with the least difference is &lt;code&gt;mv&lt;/code&gt;, which works just as it does for files:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; mkdir foo&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; mv foo/ bar/&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt; foo/&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;-bash: cd: foo: No such file or directory&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt; bar/&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Here the error message indicates that the &lt;code&gt;mv&lt;/code&gt; worked: there is no file or directory called &lt;code&gt;foo&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (The word &lt;code&gt;bash&lt;/code&gt; refers to the shell being run, in this case the “&lt;a href="https://www.gnu.org/software/bash/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Bourne Again SHell&lt;/a&gt;”.)&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The only minor subtlety is that the trailing slashes (which are typically added automatically by tab completion (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-tab_completion" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;8&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;)) are optional:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; mv bar foo&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt; foo/&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;This issue with trailing slashes never makes a difference with &lt;code&gt;mv&lt;/code&gt;, but with &lt;code&gt;cp&lt;/code&gt; it can be a source of much confusion.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In particular, when copying directories, the behavior you usually want is to copy the directory contents &lt;em&gt;including&lt;/em&gt; the directory, which on many systems requires leaving off the trailing slash.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; When copying files, you also need to include the &lt;code&gt;-r&lt;/code&gt; option (for “recursive”).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; For example, to copy the contents of the &lt;code&gt;text_files&lt;/code&gt; directory to a new directory called &lt;code&gt;foobar&lt;/code&gt;, we use the command shown in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-cp_r" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;19&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-cp_r" data-tralics-id="uid193" data-number="19"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 19:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Copying a directory.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; mkdir foobar&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt; foobar/&#x000A;&lt;span class="hll"&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; cp -r ../text_files .&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;text_files&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;Note that we’ve used &lt;code&gt;..&lt;/code&gt; to make a &lt;em&gt;relative path&lt;/em&gt;, going up one directory and then into &lt;code&gt;text_files&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Also note the &lt;em&gt;lack&lt;/em&gt; of a trailing slash in &lt;code&gt;cp -r ../text_files .&lt;/code&gt;; if we included it, we’d get &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-cp_slash" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;20&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; instead.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-cp_slash" data-tralics-id="uid194" data-number="20"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 20:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Copying with a trailing slash.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="hll"&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; cp -r ../text_files/ .&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;sonnet_1.txt     sonnet_1_reversed.txt sonnets.txt   text_files&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;In other words, &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-cp_slash" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;20&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; copies the individual files, but not the directory itself.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As a result, I recommend always omitting the trailing slash, as in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-cp_r" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;19&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;; if you want to copy only the files, be explicit using the star operator, as in:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; cp ../text_files/* .&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Unlike renaming (moving) and copying directories, which use the same &lt;code&gt;mv&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;cp&lt;/code&gt; commands used for files, in the case of removing directories there’s a dedicated command called &lt;code&gt;rmdir&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In my experience, though, it rarely works, as seen here:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; rmdir second_directory&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;rmdir: second_directory/: Directory not empty&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The error message here is what happens 99% of the time when I try to remove directories, because &lt;code&gt;rmdir&lt;/code&gt; requires the directory to be empty.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; You can of course empty it by hand (using &lt;code&gt;rm&lt;/code&gt; repeatedly), but this is frequently inconvenient, and I almost always use the more powerful (but &lt;em&gt;much&lt;/em&gt; more dangerous) “remove recursive force” command &lt;code&gt;rm -rf&lt;/code&gt;, which removes a directory, its files, and any subdirectories without confirmation (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-rm_rf" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;21&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="codelisting" id="code-rm_rf" data-tralics-id="uid195" data-number="21"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Listing 21:&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Using &lt;code&gt;rm -rf&lt;/code&gt; to remove a directory.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; rm -rf second_directory/&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; ls second_directory&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;ls: second_directory: No such file or directory&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;As the error message from &lt;code&gt;ls&lt;/code&gt; in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#code-rm_rf" class="hyperref"&gt;Listing &lt;span class="ref"&gt;21&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; indicates (“No such file or directory”), our use of &lt;code&gt;rm -rf&lt;/code&gt; succeeded in removing the directory.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The powerful command &lt;code&gt;rm -rf&lt;/code&gt; is too convenient to ignore, but remember: “&lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uncle_Ben#.22With_great_power_comes_great_responsibility.22" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;With great power comes great responsibility&lt;/a&gt;” (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-spider_man" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;22&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;sup id="cha-0_footnote-ref-28" class="footnote"&gt;&lt;a href="#cha-0_footnote-28"&gt;28&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="center figure" id="fig-spider_man" data-tralics-id="uid197" data-number="22"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="graphics image"&gt;&lt;img src="images/figures/spider_man.jpg" alt="images/figures/spider_man"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Figure 22: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;This &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spider-Man" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;superhero&lt;/a&gt; understands how to use the power of &lt;code&gt;rm -rf&lt;/code&gt; responsibly.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-grep_redux" data-tralics-id="uid198" class="subsubsection" data-number="4.4.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-grep_redux" class="heading"&gt;Grep redux&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Now that we know a little about directories, we are in a position to add a useful &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; variation to our toolkit from &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-grepping" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3.4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As with &lt;code&gt;cp&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;rm&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt; takes a “recursive” option, &lt;code&gt;-r&lt;/code&gt;, which in this case greps through a directory’s files and the files in its subdirectories.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This is incredibly useful when you’re looking for a string in a file somewhere in a hierarchy of directories, but you’re not sure where the file is.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Here’s the setup, which puts the word “&lt;a href="http://dictionary.reference.com/browse/sesquipedalian" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;sesquipedalian&lt;/a&gt;” in a file called &lt;code&gt;long_word.txt&lt;/code&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt; text_files/&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; mkdir foo&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt; foo/&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;echo&lt;/span&gt; sesquipedalian &amp;gt; long_word.txt&#x000A;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class="nb"&gt;cd&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The final &lt;code&gt;cd&lt;/code&gt; puts us back in the home directory.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Suppose we now want to find the file containing “sesquipedalian”.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; The way &lt;em&gt;not&lt;/em&gt; to do it is this:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; grep sesquipedalian text_files    &lt;span class="c1"&gt;# This doesn&#x0027;t work.&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;grep: text_files: Is a directory&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Here &lt;code&gt;grep&lt;/code&gt;’s error message indicates that the command didn’t work, but adding &lt;code&gt;-r&lt;/code&gt; does the trick:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; grep -r sesquipedalian text_files&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;text_files/foo/long_word.txt:sesquipedalian&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Because case rarely matters, I recommend making a habit of adding the &lt;code&gt;-i&lt;/code&gt; option when grepping recursively, as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="code"&gt;&lt;div class="highlight"&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="gp"&gt;$&lt;/span&gt; grep -ri sesquipedalian text_files&#x000A;&lt;span class="go"&gt;text_files/foo/long_word.txt:sesquipedalian&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Armed with &lt;code&gt;grep -ri&lt;/code&gt;, we are now equipped to find strings of our choice in arbitrarily deep hierarchies of directories.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_mv_cp_rmdir" data-tralics-id="uid199" class="subsubsection" data-number="4.4.2"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_mv_cp_rmdir" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Make a directory &lt;code&gt;foo&lt;/code&gt; with a subdirectory &lt;code&gt;bar&lt;/code&gt;, then rename the subdirectory to &lt;code&gt;baz&lt;/code&gt;. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-mkdir-sub-rm"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Copy all the files in &lt;code&gt;text_files&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;em&gt;with&lt;/em&gt; directory, into &lt;code&gt;foo&lt;/code&gt;. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-copy-recursive"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Copy all the files in &lt;code&gt;text_files&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;em&gt;without&lt;/em&gt; directory, into &lt;code&gt;bar&lt;/code&gt;. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-copy-not-recursive"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Remove &lt;code&gt;foo&lt;/code&gt; and everything in it using a single command. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-rm-dir"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-summary_directories" data-tralics-id="uid204" class="subsection" data-number="4.5"&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-summary_directories" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;4.5 &lt;/span&gt;Summary&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Important commands from this section are summarized in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#table-directories" class="hyperref"&gt;Table &lt;span class="ref"&gt;6&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="table-directories" data-tralics-id="uid205" data-number="6" class="table"&gt;&lt;table class="tabular"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr class="bottom_border"&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Command&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Description&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Example&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;mkdir &amp;lt;name&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Make directory with name&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ mkdir foo&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;pwd&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Print working directory&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ pwd&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;cd &amp;lt;dir&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Change to &amp;lt;dir&amp;gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ cd foo/&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;cd ~/&amp;lt;dir&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;cd relative to home&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ cd ~/foo/&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;cd&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Change to home directory&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ cd&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;cd -&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Change to previous directory&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ cd &amp;amp;&amp;amp; pwd &amp;amp;&amp;amp; cd -&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;.&lt;/code&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;The current directory&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ cp ~/foo.txt .&lt;/code&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;..&lt;/code&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;One directory up&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ cd ..&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;find&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Find files &amp;amp; directories&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ find .&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; -name foo*.*&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;cp -r &amp;lt;old&amp;gt; &amp;lt;new&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Copy recursively&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ cp -r ~/foo .&lt;/code&gt;&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;rmdir &amp;lt;dir&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Remove (empty) dir&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ rmdir foo/&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;rm -rf &amp;lt;dir&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Remove dir &amp;amp; contents&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ rm -rf foo/&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code class="tt"&gt;grep -ri &amp;lt;string&amp;gt; &amp;lt;dir&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;Grep recursively (case-insensitive)&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;td class="align_left"&gt;&lt;code&gt;$ grep -ri foo bar/&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;div class="caption"&gt;&lt;span class="header"&gt;Table 6: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Important commands from &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-directories" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;4&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&#x000A;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div id="sec-exercises_summary_directories" data-tralics-id="uid206" class="subsubsection" data-number="4.5.1"&gt;&lt;h4&gt;&lt;a href="#sec-exercises_summary_directories" class="heading"&gt;Exercises&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;&lt;div class="society-note"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Solutions to exercises are available for free at &lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/solutions" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/solutions&lt;/a&gt; with any Learn Enough purchase.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To see other people’s answers and to record your own, join the &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Learn Enough Society&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/society" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;learnenough.com/society&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Starting in your home directory, execute a single command-line command to make a directory &lt;code&gt;foo&lt;/code&gt;, change into it, create a file &lt;code&gt;bar&lt;/code&gt; with content “baz”, print out &lt;code&gt;bar&lt;/code&gt;’s contents, and then &lt;code&gt;cd&lt;/code&gt; back to the directory you came from.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: Combine the commands as described in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-combining_commands" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;12&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-combined-commands"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;What happens when you run the previous command again?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; How many of the commands executed?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Why? &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-combined-commands-again"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;Explain why the command &lt;code&gt;rm -rf /&lt;/code&gt; is unbelievably dangerous, and why you should never type it into a terminal window, not even as a joke. &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-rm-f-danger"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;How can the previous command be made even more dangerous?&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: Refer to &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-sudo" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;11&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (This command is so dangerous you shouldn’t even &lt;em&gt;think&lt;/em&gt; it, much less type it.) &lt;span class="exercise" id="ex-rm-f-more-danger"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="sec-conclusion" data-tralics-id="cid5" class="section" data-number="5"&gt;&lt;h2&gt;&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-conclusion" class="heading hyperref"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;5 &lt;/span&gt;Conclusion&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Congratulations!&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; You’ve officially learned enough command line to be &lt;em&gt;dangerous&lt;/em&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Of course, this is only one step on a longer journey, both toward command-line excellence (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-additional_resources" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;13&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) and software development wizardry.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As you proceed on this journey, you will probably discover that learning computer magic can be exciting and empowering, but it can also be &lt;em&gt;hard&lt;/em&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Indeed, you may already have discovered this fact, either on your own or while doing this tutorial.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; To those brave magicians-in-training who wish to proceed, I offer the following sequence, which is currently in preparation:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Developer Fundamentals&lt;/strong&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;&lt;a Dangerous&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/git-tutorial" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Learn Enough Git to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Web Basics&lt;/strong&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;&lt;a
