href="http://www.learnenough.com/css-and-layout-tutorial" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Learn Enough CSS &amp;amp; Layout to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/javascript-tutorial" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Learn Enough JavaScript to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Intro Ruby Web Development&lt;/strong&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/ruby-tutorial" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Learn Enough Ruby to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/sinatra-tutorial" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Learn Enough Sinatra to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.learnenough.com/ruby-on-rails-tutorial" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Learn Enough Ruby on Rails to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Professional Ruby Web Development&lt;/strong&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ul&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.railstutorial.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;The Ruby on Rails Tutorial&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;Only the first three titles and the last title in the above list are complete, but all the other links go to landing pages where you can sign up to be notified when the next tutorial in the sequence is ready.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; See you there!&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;div class="aside" id="aside-additional_resources" data-tralics-id="uid225" data-number="13"&gt;&lt;div class="heading"&gt;&lt;span class="number"&gt;Box 13.&lt;/span&gt; &#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;span class="description"&gt;Additional resources&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;I recommend following the &lt;em&gt;Learn Enough&lt;/em&gt; sequence, as it represents the shortest path to technical proficiency and software development skills, but at some point you’ll probably want to expand your command-line skills as well.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; When that time comes, I recommend consulting this list, which consists mainly of resources recommended by readers of the present tutorial:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;ul&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href="http://conqueringthecommandline.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Conquering the Command Line&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt; book and screencasts by Mark Bates (which like the present tutorial is available for free &lt;a href="http://conqueringthecommandline.com/book" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;online&lt;/a&gt;)&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.edx.org/course/introduction-linux-linuxfoundationx-lfs101x-2" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;edX course on Linux&lt;/a&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.codecademy.com/learn/learn-the-command-line" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Codecademy course on the command line&lt;/a&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;The similarly named &lt;a href="http://cli.learncodethehardway.org/book/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;The Command Line Crash Course&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="http://www.vikingcodeschool.com/web-development-basics/a-command-line-crash-course" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;A Command Line Crash Course&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href="http://linuxcommand.org/lc3_learning_the_shell.php" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Learning the Shell&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&#x000A;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;small&gt;&lt;/small&gt;&lt;small&gt;&lt;em&gt;Learn Enough Command Line to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/small&gt;&lt;small&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Copyright © 2015 by Michael Hartl.&lt;/small&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;If you enjoyed this tutorial, please &lt;a href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/B01KG84X44" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;leave a review at Amazon&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Thanks!&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="cha-0_footnotes"&gt;&#x000A;  &lt;ol class="footnotes"&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-1"&gt;As discussed in &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-basics" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, this statement applies to the &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/esr/writings/taoup/html/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Unix tradition&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, which is the principal computing tradition behind the Internet and the World Wide Web, and the tradition followed by this tutorial.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In addition to being important for developers, knowing the command line is also essential for &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/System_administrator" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;system administrators&lt;/a&gt; (sysadmins). &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-1"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-2"&gt;In a fairly typical turn of events, the name &lt;em&gt;Unix&lt;/em&gt; started as a &lt;a href="http://www.catb.org/jargon/html/U/Unix.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;pun&lt;/a&gt; on a rival system called &lt;em&gt;Multics&lt;/em&gt;. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-2"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-3"&gt;An IDE, or &lt;em&gt;integrated development environment&lt;/em&gt;, integrates several development tools (such as a command line and a text editor) into one application. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-3"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-4"&gt;An option is sometimes also called a &lt;em&gt;flag&lt;/em&gt;. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-4"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-5"&gt;For example, when developing web applications, in addition to my main command-line tab I often have separate tabs for running a &lt;a href="https://www.railstutorial.org/book/beginning#sec-rails_server" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;local web server&lt;/a&gt; and an &lt;a href="https://www.railstutorial.org/book/static_pages#sec-our_first_test" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;automated test suite&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-5"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-6"&gt;There are subtle differences between the two cases, but they aren’t important at the level of this tutorial.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Use your technical sophistication (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#aside-technical_sophistication" class="hyperref"&gt;Box &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) if you’re curious.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;em&gt;Hint&lt;/em&gt;: &lt;a href="http://lmgtfy.com/?q=command+line+shell+single+double+quote+differences" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Google searches&lt;/a&gt; are your friends. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-6"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-7"&gt;Image retrieved from https://www.flickr.com/photos/pheezy/5875298232 on 2015-07-19.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Copyright © 2011 by Evan P. Cordes and used unaltered under the terms of the &lt;a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/2.0/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Creative Commons Attribution 2.0 Generic&lt;/a&gt; license. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-7"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-8"&gt;Many introductions to the command line cover elements of the shell that require knowledge of a text editor—knowledge which (as noted in the introduction) this tutorial does &lt;em&gt;not&lt;/em&gt; assume.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As a result, we’ll defer these important topics to the follow-on tutorials to this one (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-conclusion" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;5&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), starting with &lt;a href="http://learnenough.com/text-editor-tutorial" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Learn Enough Text Editor to Be Dangerous&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-8"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-9"&gt;Image retrieved from https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Jazz_at_Knicks_man_to_man_defense.jpg on 2015-07-22.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Copyright © 2005 by Lordcolus and used unaltered under the terms of the &lt;a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/2.0/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Creative Commons Attribution 2.0 Generic&lt;/a&gt; license. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-9"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-10"&gt;Copyright © Randall Munroe and used unaltered under the terms of the &lt;a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc/2.5/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Creative Commons Attribution-NonCommercial 2.5 Generic&lt;/a&gt; license. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-10"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-11"&gt;There are also commands for moving one &lt;em&gt;word&lt;/em&gt; at a time (&lt;code class="tt"&gt;ESC F&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code class="tt"&gt;ESC B&lt;/code&gt;), but I hardly ever use them myself, so it’s clear they are not required to be &lt;em&gt;dangerous&lt;/em&gt;. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-11"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-12"&gt;Note that the &lt;a href="http://originalpronunciation.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Original Pronunciation&lt;/a&gt; (OP) of Shakespearean English is different from modern pronunciation.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Generally speaking, Shakespeare’s sonnets include many word pairs that don’t rhyme in modern English but do in OP.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; In the case of &lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-sonnet_1" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;12&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, the word “memory” should be pronounced “MEM-or-aye”, leading to a rhyme between lines 2 and 4 (ending in &lt;em&gt;die&lt;/em&gt; and &lt;em&gt;memory&lt;/em&gt;, respectively).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Image retrieved from https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Sonnet_1.jpg on 2015-07-20.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This work is in the public domain and can be used without restriction. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-12"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-13"&gt;Some keyboards lack an Option key, so obviously this trick won’t work on such systems. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-13"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-14"&gt;Image retrieved from https://www.flickr.com/photos/tiffanyday/4076289684 on 2015-07-22.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Copyright 2009 by Tiffa Day and used unaltered under the terms of the &lt;a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/2.0/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Creative Commons Attribution 2.0 Generic&lt;/a&gt; license. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-14"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-15"&gt;&lt;p&gt;From the essay “&lt;a href="http://www.paulgraham.com/say.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;What You Can’t Say&lt;/a&gt;” by &lt;a href="http://paulgraham.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Paul Graham&lt;/a&gt; (2004).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; As Graham &lt;a href="http://www.paulgraham.com/saynotes.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;notes&lt;/a&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;blockquote class="quotation"&gt;&#x000A;&lt;p&gt;The verb “diff” is computer jargon, but it’s the only word with exactly the sense I want.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; It comes from the Unix &lt;code class="tt"&gt;diff&lt;/code&gt; utility, which yields a list of all the differences between two files.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; More generally it means an unselective and microscopically thorough comparison between two versions of something.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/blockquote&gt; &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-15"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-16"&gt;A &lt;em&gt;bit&lt;/em&gt; is one piece of yes-or-no information (such as a 1 or a 0), and a &lt;em&gt;byte&lt;/em&gt; is eight bits.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Bytes are probably most familiar from “megabytes” and “gigabytes”, which represent a million and a billion bytes, respectively.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; (The &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megabyte" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;official story&lt;/a&gt; is a little more complicated, but level of detail here is certainly enough to be &lt;em&gt;dangerous&lt;/em&gt;.) &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-16"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-17"&gt;URL is short for &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uniform_Resource_Locator" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Uniform Resource Locator&lt;/a&gt;, and in practice usually just means “web address”. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-17"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-18"&gt;&lt;a href="https://m.xkcd.com/1475/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Technically&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;code&gt;which&lt;/code&gt; locates a file on the user’s &lt;em&gt;path&lt;/em&gt;, which is a list of directories where executable programs are located. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-18"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-19"&gt;If for any reason using &lt;code&gt;curl&lt;/code&gt; fails, you can always visit the URL in a browser and the use &lt;strong&gt;File &amp;gt; Save As&lt;/strong&gt; feature to save it to your local disk. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-19"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-20"&gt;Having known about &lt;code&gt;ls -a&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;ls -rtl&lt;/code&gt; for a while—which together yield the suggestive command &lt;code&gt;ls -artl&lt;/code&gt;—one day I decided to add an “h”’ (for &lt;a href="http://mhartl.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;obvious reasons&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; This is actually how I accidentally discovered the useful &lt;code&gt;-h&lt;/code&gt; option some years ago. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-20"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-21"&gt;On some systems, apparently they’re &lt;a href="http://unix.stackexchange.com/questions/604/isnt-less-just-more" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;exactly the same program&lt;/a&gt;, so &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt; really is &lt;code&gt;more&lt;/code&gt; (or, more accurately, &lt;code&gt;more&lt;/code&gt; is &lt;code&gt;less&lt;/code&gt;). &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-21"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-22"&gt;Image retrieved from https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Tudor_Rose.svg on 2015-07-21.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Copyright © 2011 by Sodacan and used unaltered under the &lt;a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/2.0/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Creative Commons Attribution-ShareAlike 2.0 Generic&lt;/a&gt; license. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-22"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-23"&gt;Although Shakespeare’s sonnets are undated, most of them were probably composed during the reign of &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Queen Elizabeth&lt;/a&gt;, whose &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tudor_dynasty" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;royal house&lt;/a&gt; adopted a rose (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#fig-tudor_rose" class="hyperref"&gt;Figure &lt;span class="ref"&gt;18&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) as its &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heraldry" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;heraldic emblem&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Given this context, Shakespeare’s choice of floral imagery isn’t surprising, but in fact only a few commentators on the &lt;em&gt;Sonnets&lt;/em&gt; have &lt;a href="https://hankwhittemore.wordpress.com/tag/sonnet-1/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;noticed&lt;/a&gt; the seemingly obvious reference. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-23"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-24"&gt;It comes from “&lt;strong&gt;g&lt;/strong&gt;lobally search a &lt;strong&gt;r&lt;/strong&gt;egular &lt;strong&gt;e&lt;/strong&gt;xpression and &lt;strong&gt;p&lt;/strong&gt;rint”, but &lt;a href="http://www.urbandictionary.com/define.php?term=slartibartfast" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;I told you it wasn’t important&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-24"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-25"&gt;Actually, “ROSE”, “RoSE”, “rOSE”, etc., all match as well, but “Rose” is the likeliest candidate.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Confirming this hunch is left as an exercise (&lt;a href="command_line_fragment.html#sec-exercises_grep" class="hyperref"&gt;Section &lt;span class="ref"&gt;3.4.1&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;). &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-25"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-26"&gt;Copyright © Randall Munroe and used unaltered under the terms of the &lt;a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc/2.5/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Creative Commons Attribution-NonCommercial 2.5 Generic&lt;/a&gt; license. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-26"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-27"&gt;My directory has a huge number of text files, ’cause that’s just how I roll, so the command I ran was actually &lt;code&gt;find .&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; -name ’*.txt’ | grep text_files&lt;/code&gt;, which filters out anything that doesn’t match the directory being used in this tutorial. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-27"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;    &lt;li id="cha-0_footnote-28"&gt;Image retrieved from https://www.flickr.com/photos/whatleydude/13950241545 on 2015-07-22.&lt;span class="intersentencespace"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; Copyright © 2014 by James Whatley and used unaltered under the terms of the &lt;a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/2.0/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Creative Commons Attribution 2.0 Generic&lt;/a&gt; license. &lt;a class="arrow" href="#cha-0_footnote-ref-28"&gt;↑&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&#x000A;  &lt;/ol&gt;&#x000A;&lt;/div&gt;' id='j_sectionContent'></div>
</div>

Save As\u003c/strong\u003e feature to save it to your local disk. ","cha-0_footnote-20":"Having known about \u003ccode\u003els -a\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003els -rtl\u003c/code\u003e for a rel=\"noopener\"\u003eobvious reasons\u003c/a\u003e).\u003cspan class=\"intersentencespace\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e This is actually how I accidentally discovered the useful \u003ccode\u003e-h\u003c/code\u003e option some years ago. ","cha-0_footnote-21":"On some systems, apparently they’re \u003ca href=\"http://unix.stackexchange.com/questions/604/isnt-less-just-more\"
